<Author>sindoria
<Content>Not worth the money We stayed at the resort the week between christmas and New Years. We had mixed feelings about our stay at the resort.On the one hand the resort is away from it all and is a good place to relax and unwind, on the other hand the facilities at the resort especailly the accomodations could use some face lifting.Focusing on the good things, the pools are great, there are enough activities to keep kids busy for a few days. The resort is close to some of the nicer beaches we have seen in Puerto Rico.On the flip side the accomodations are just bad compared to the money being charged. A Super 8 motel would have better accomodations than these guys. If your idea of accomodations is a squeaky iron bed on wheels with a really old uncomfortable matterss then this is the place for you. The TV's are the small RCA TV's from I dont even know when. I also dont see any reason for paying more for ocean view rooms as opposed to garden view...I dont really see the difference since there are only two floors in the buildings. The resort is away from it all so be prepared to pay top dollar for the two on site restaurants.Summing it up we think that the resort is really not worth the money , if you really want to explore the beautiful beaches in this section of puerto rico there might be better places to stay.

<Author>udalum
<Content>A Pretty Good Stay Location: This hotel was located in Guanica, and was surrounded by a large park with a lot of hiking. The beach was pretty good. There was not much visibility to snorkel from the beach. Since the water was clalm, it was quite easy to swim in the ocean. There was lots of seaweed on the bottom, so sand shoes are recommended. The people at the hotel speak English, but many of the surrounding areas do not. We speak passable Spanish, so we did not have a problem.The rooms: The rooms were fairly big, and allow room to spread out. The beds were uncomfortable for me and my spouse, because anytime one of us moved, the other felt it, and woke up. The rooms were quite quiet. I saw a cockroach once in the room, which grossed me out. I would expect this to happen, though. The restaurant: We ate at the cheaper restaurant just one night. The food was just o.k., and was quite overpriced for the quality. Gilligan's Island: The island was just a short boat ride away. The visibility for snorkeling was just fair. I was able to see a needlenose fish, a puffer fish, and some other fish. We did not like hanging out here too long, because we like to lay on a beach and get some sun. There was not a lot of room for that. I was unimpressed with this island.The Hiking: It was interesting, but very similar to what we have seen in Arizona. Day Trips: We went to Arecibo, and tried to see the caves. It was unclear whether the caves would be open or not, and they ended up not being open. To get there, we took the mountain route through the center of the country. It was nice for the first few minutes, but after that time it was long an repetitive. We drove back to the hotel by using the route that circled the west part of the island. That route was full of strip shopping malls. I would not recommend making the trip to see just Arecibo, unless someone was really interested in space. We also visited Ponce and El German. Ponce was a little dumpy for us. El German was much more quaint. Who would be happy here?: I would say don't make the trip to the southwest of the island unless you are an avid hiker who would explore the park at Guanica, and other hiking areas close by. Also, it is important to know some passable Spanish.

<Author>JackieElla
<Content>Copamarina Soothed the Cranky Traveler I will start this review by saying that my daughter and I call my husband The cranky traveler. He pretty much hates the process of travel and it takes him days to get in the groove of the vacation. That was not the case at Copamarina. He instantly fell in love with the casual, peaceful atmosphere and the beautiful grounds and pools. I had to literally drag him out of the jacuzzi when it was time for dinner. We both truly enjoyed the food and the ambience. Our room was clean and comfortable (we had a Deluxe Ocean View room), and management was very responsive with the few requests that we had (extra pillows, etc.)We tend to be pool people, not beach people, so we didn't have an issue with the beach as some people seem to have. However, during our stay, there were people on the beach having a great time.We are avid golfers and took two days to play at the new 18 hole course in Ponce - Costa Caribe. Heaven!We will go back in 09 as this may well be our new favorite escape.

<Author>olde_tyme_style
<Content>Paradise Found It has been quite a while since I stayed at the Copamarina, but the memories are so vibrant that it seems like it was just yesterday...If you are looking for a secluded tropical atmosphere, than this is the resort for you. On the southwestern side of the island, you are almost a 3 hour car ride from the hustle and bustle of San Juan. The property grounds are expansive and quiet and the property is on a white sand beachfront that is very clean. What I really loved is that scattered about the property are aviaries with beautiful parrots inside. Some of the aviaries are larger than others. The parrots did not make any noises that would disturb guests. Matter of fact, they were much quieter than the guests. I would have liked to see the parrots have more activities in their cages because some looked bored and some looked like they were in too small of cages and like they existed solely for their beauty and not their comfort.The room I stayed in was nice. It was on the ground floor of a two story building. There was a nice door that opened to the gardens with tropical flowers that I enjoyed. The garden door had a top and a bottom that can be opened in two different pieces for a nice ocean breeze if you choose. The decor was nice too. It was not top of the line, but in good condition, tropical and pretty. The bathroom had a few small rogue ants on the counter that most likely came in through an open window near the ceiling. I really dislike bugs, but the ants did not bother me at all and I was able to quickly get rid of them and I don't remember them coming back after that. There was a fantastic ocean view from the room when the garden door was open. The grounds were well maintained.The housekeeping staff did a nice job at maintaining the room during my stay and the public areas were kept clean too. The cleaning staff mops the terra cotta tile in the common area outside the front of the room early in the morning so be careful, I slipped and fell on the wet floor, but was ok so just laughed it off. I needed to use the laundry machine and I don't recomend it for delicate garments because it ripped an item, but overall no biggie - I didn't have a garmet bag for the wash as I would at home.The beach was amazing and I did many watersports. I took an aqua cycle, kayak and a water scooter and had a great time. I didn't think these were included in the price of my stay since I didn't go all-inclusive, but didn't get charged extra for these when I checked out. There were great lounge chairs sunk partially into the ocean that were so memorable to me. It was such a greta experience to be lounging in the late afternoon sun and have gentle waves washing up on the seat of the lounger to cool me down. The water was so blue and was never rough surf.The restaurant was tasty. Breakfast had a variety of hot and cold items and was included because I booked using the Puerto Rico Is Fun package. I don't know if the country's tourism department still promotes tourism with this package. I did dinner at least one night and remember having a tender fillet with baked plantain chips garnished with caribbean fruits-yum! If you are looking for a relaxing vacation or a vacation where you can be in touch with nature in the ocean or at the dry forest nearby than this is for you. I am not a surfer, but nearby in Rincon there is great surfing and beaches, although becoming increasingly popular since my stay. If you would like to leave the resort to explore I recomend a car rental since you are in a secluded area of the island. There was also a bioluminescent bay in Llajas where you can take a boatride to see. It was threatened by boat pollution 6 years ago so I don;t know if you can still see it. Llajas is a very small town with friendly people. If you are not comfortable with this type of environment than the boatride might not be for you.I didn't want to leave and tried to extend my stay on the day I checked out, but the resort was booked solid. Locals sometimes come to stay at the resort to enjoy themselves because it is so beautiful and offers many fun amenities.

<Author>NatureDude
<Content>Copamarina good value but skip the beach Since this resort has a lot of mixed reviews I thought I'd add our experience. First, the staff was great and upgraded us without asking to a suite at the end of a building so it had views on 3 sides. The room was great with nice if a bit cheap furniture, comfortable bed, sitting area, etc. The resort grounds are very nice with typical tropical resort landscaping and a nice newer pool at one end. The restaurant and bar are also quite nice. The resort is well patronized by Puerto Ricans as we were possibly the only gringos there at the time but we still felt very welcome. Now for the negative part: the beach is not conducive to laying out or swimming. It is a very biologically-active beach so we're talking muck that smells like raw sewage making it rather unpleasant to try to lay out within 30 feet of it let alone swim near shore. The owners claim it is a bioreserve and so the intact sea grass beds create this situation. That is fine but it is not a pleasant beach atmosphere. The swimming beach a short walk away is a public park beach that we found littered with garbage and excrement and it has an extremely steep profile so waves break right on it making it unsuitable for swimming especially for children. The cove however is really nice and we rented a hobie cat and had a great sail. While we were there a sunken boat was blocking the way to Giligan's Island so we could not get there, perhaps that has been cleared by now. I would still recommend this resort as a good value with nice amenities but I'd drive somewhere else for beaches.

<Content>Peaceful, Idyllic, Serene My husband and I stayed at Copamarina for my birthday - and what a perfect gift it was. <Author>Coqui55
<Content>Not Worth the Money Since the Hilton at Ponce was booked we opted to stay at the Copamarina because of the proximity to Ponce and that the resort listed beach front. Although the room rates were somewhat high I figured that the hotel/resort would be worth the stay. Was I wrong! The room is old and in need of renovation. The beds are hard and horrible. Not comfortable at all. The A/C unit did not work properly, it was barely 75 degrees in the room. The TV did not have a good reception. I informed the front desk of these problems and none were corrected. I was offered another room, however when I checked the other room the A/C had the same problem, and the room wasn't any better. The beach was horrible! A public beach is a few hundred yards away and the swimming there is awesome, the water is clean. Yet, at the Copamarina the water and sand is disgusting. The resort nickles and dimes you for everything, even a short trip to a nearby island. (The Conquistador in Fajordo has a private island and they don't charge you to take you there). When you go check out the beach towels you are immediatley told that there is a $15.00 dollar fee per towel if you don't return them. If you want to take a kayak there is a fee. There is nothing for free!!! And the resort charges too much to stay there!. The restaurant, The Alexandra, is rated five stars. However, when we ate there the food was horrible. My sister-in-law and my husband ordered the same dish, the shrimps were hard. My sister-in-law's husband ordered a New York Strip and was brought another type of meat that was hard and dry. The food took forever to reach the table. While we made reservations for 8:30pm, ordered crab cakes (which were horrible), it an hour to get our food. And the restuarant was not full. The waitress was less than pleasing. In addition, when I got my credit card bill the Copamarina charged me additonal for unknown reason, which I am disputing. I would not recommed this hotel to anyone. If you can't find somthing in Ponce keep going. Save your money. And I agree with the last entry, the reception desk was less than friendly when I told them the problems that we had experienced. Even thought I had spoken to the same person on the phone about the room's A/C and TV problems he asked me upon check out if I had reported these problems.

<Author>snorkeltime
<Content>Both good and bad We stayed at the Copamarina for spring break along with another family in April of this year. Our kids ranged form ages 9 to 18. When we got back I sat down and wrote a long and negative review and then accidentally erased it. Now that some time has passed my thoughts are less negative. Hopefully this review will be helpful.I'll start with the good:  1)The grounds are emmaculate - reminded me of Hawaii. These grounds are definitely the pride and joy of the owner. 2) Alexanders was wonderful dining. However fast service does not exist - expect your dinner there to last at least 2 hours. 3) The dive shop was very helpful. We went to Gilligan's island on a ferry and we snorkeled on a sand key off shore from the Copamarina. Both fun excursions that we booked through the dive shop.4) The wait staff and bar tenders were all delightful. very attentive even when busy. Try the Mojita's--the best I've ever had!Now the bad:1)Housekeeping in the rooms was minimal. The bathroom floor and shower walls had many hairs and other ick on it from previous guests. I finally just wiped the walls down myself.2)Our toilet overflowed all over one afternoon. I called the front desk and requested engineering followed by housekeeping. We then left and returned to our room in the evening. Engineering had come and fixed the toilet. They also used all of our towels to mop up the floor, leaving them in a heap in the middle of the bathroom. I called the front desk to enquire about housekeeping. I was told housekeeping was told to come and now they were gone for the night so nothing more could be done. I asked for new towels so I could line the dirty floor with clean towels. I was told that only housekeeping had a key to the lilinen room and again they were gone. After much insisting the evening manager finally agreed to get clean towles out of an empty room if I would come pick them up. When I picked up the towels he also gave me a bottle of disinfectant so I could clean the floor myself!! I spoke with the main manager the next day and was given an apology and that was it.3)Two in our party got food poisoning from the outdoor restaraunt. 4)The beach is pretty at high tide but not very nice to walk or play in. It basically was made of areas of clay and sea grass. Luckily the island is full of many other beautiful beaches.Would I go back to the Copamarina?? Definitely not.Would I go back to Puerto Rico? Most definitely. The countryside was beautiful with lots to do and the local people were very nice. We felt very safe driving around and exploring!

<Author>miiaoww
<Content>Wonderful Stay for Relaxing or Being Active My husband and I stayed here for our honeymoon and we absolutely loved it. We did the all-inclusive, which covered all our meals and drinks, and non-motorized water sports. I do think that whether it's a good fit for you really depends on what you expect. We loved the fact that this is not in a high-traffic, highly-touristy area. We chose to go here because we could stay longer and do what we liked more easily than at other more expensive resorts. We don't golf (there's no golf course). We don't gamble (there's no casino). We don't go clubbing (there are no clubs - there's not much of anything else nearby, really). We swim, sail, kayak, snorkle, eat, sleep, and read. If you want a pool boy to put a drink in your hand, you should look somewhere else, but we are very independent and found this to be a perfect fit, from the beach to the restaurant to the room. Our room was not fancy but it was very comfortable. For those of you who don't want to make a complete break with the outside world, there is cable TV and wireless internet access. (We were pleased to find this when it rained one afternoon.) It is really a pretty place. The view from our balcony was amazing. We loved the water. There is some sort of sea grass growing right around the dock in front of the resort, but we pulled lounge chairs into the warm sea - ahhh. For a swim, we walked a ways towards the public beach, where the sandy bottom extended quite a distance. My husband was a big fan of both swimming pools and the hot tub. We also spent an entire afternoon lounging in one of the beachside beds, under the canvas canopy, reading.But what excited us most of all were the active options. Two days, we took out the little sail boat and skirted all around the bay. We paddled the kayak one afternoon. Towards the end of the trip we went snorkeling at Gilligan's Island. You do have to hit the dive shop early to get snorkeling gear - there's a limited amount and it gets checked out pretty fast. Take a few dollars - you'll need to pay the ferry boat guy who stops at the resort dock. Gilligan's Island is a small, uninhabited park. Its main lagoon gets crowded on the weekend, but we went off to a secluded spot on the side and saw some beautiful fish.We put on nice clothes and ate at the Alexandra restaurant every night. Our waiters were really pleasant and attentive. We tried just about everything on the menu, and thought every dish was nice and some were superb. (The steak with red wine sauce and the lobster risotto were tops.) The breakfast was extensive and changed throughout the week: yummy crepes one day, waffles the next. Lunches and appetizers at the bar were just fine but nothing exceptional, although the guitarist playing live music in the evening was a nice touch. I love cheese, and the local Puerto Rican cheese was a delicious discovery. True, there's no room service, but they will give you box lunches or pack up whatever you like.It was very quiet during the week, and there were families and locals on the weekend. It seemed very friendly to children. There's even a nice playground sliding-board set under some palm trees. An exceptional example: Our last night, we ate very late when the restaurant was almost completely empty. We watched a young, frazzled couple drop into the Alexandra and ask for to-go meals, because they feared their little girl was fussy. One of the waitresses offered to babysit in the empty side dining area, and spent the next hour nearby singing softly, dancing gently to the music, and showing off the fish in the fishtank. That waitress truly went far beyond what was expected, and the parents got to have what must have been their first romantic dinner alone in two years.What else should I add? There's no passport required for US citizens to go to Puerto Rico, they use the US dollar, and most people speak English but life will be even easier if you speak a little Spanish. I don't think there is any laundry service, but we were very happy to discover a coin-operated washer and dryer. We went into La Parguera to see the bioluminescent bay one evening - it was cool, and I'm glad we did it, but it's an expensive cab fare and that's the only thing worth doing there (the town is rather rundown, there was nothing to see, and the food at the resort was better than anything there). Our bathroom had a huge tiled shower but no bathtub - not a problem for us at all, but I imagine some people would find that a turn-off...All in all, we had a great stay and would return any time.

<Author>Gburger
<Content>Very Nice Setting My wife and I stayed at the Copamarina in April of 2008, for our 25th wedding anniversary. We had read all the reviews and it is funny how there are such conflicting opinions. In general we agreed that the resort is a beautiful setting, but the food leaves much to be desired.One of our main complaints was that even though the resort was almost empty, we were assigned to a room right by the noisy ice machines and maid closet, plus we were directly adjacent (with a shared connecting door) to a large group of young people who obvioulsy went out partying each night (not at the resort) until 3:00am and came home very boisterous. The walls are very thin, so it felt like they were in our room. It made no senss to us that we were not 'spread out'. After the 2nd night, we asked to be moved, and we were accommodated immediately, with no questions asked (we should have asked earlier).Back to the food, we don't consider ourselves food snobs by any means, but we rated the resturants as mediocre. Also, the first night at Alexandra's, we mentioned casually to the matre'd that we had not yet been visited by the waiter, after about 10-15 minutes (we just wanted to place a drink order since it was so nice sitting outside by the pool). Th waiter then showed up, obviously perturbed at our impatience, and rudely asked what we wanted to order, since he assumed we were in a hurry. We explained that we were not in a hurry, just wanted a drink. By the end of the evening we were on chummy terms with him, so it turned out OK.The drive from San Juan took longer than expected, but it is very scenic, and that was the only 'sightseeing' that we did, since we generally did not want to leave the resort, since it is so pleasant and restful.We did the Gilligan's Island trip - definetly over-rated, I'm sad to say. It is very small and very few areas to sit on the beach.We found the service at the resort to be very good, with everyone very friendly (we opted for the all-inclusive plan, so we got to know the wait staff well by the end of our stay). Not sure if the all-inclusive is worth it - you have to eat/drink a lot to justify it. Plus, tips are not included, which adds to the overall cost and makes it harder to justify. I definetly disagree with that policy - I think most all-inclusives include tips. But honestly, we did have a good time and would recommend this resort for a relaxing get-away.  
<Date>May 14, 2008

<Author>russell1985
<Content>Great getaway, needs a little more service I went to the Copamarina for my honeymoon. This is a great estate, situated on a really remote portion of Puerto Rico (a 2 1/2 hour drive from San Juan International Airport). The landscaping and scenery are second to none, my new wife and I loved all of the beautiful scenery and the laid back atmosphere. However, we did feel a few crucial pieces were missing to give this resort a better grade. First there is NO room service, so do not plan on taking a morning off and just relaxing in the room. You must go down to one of the two restaurants to get your meals. Another drawback was there is no honor bar or wet bar. So, you cannot continue a party back in your room or enjoy a nightcap before bed without going down to the bar and grabbing another drink, which is quite a walk I might add, especially if you're on the second floor of building three. These are minor drawbacks, but when you pay that much money for an all - inclusive package, I expect some of these extras to be there, and when they are not it is disappointing. All in all we had a good time. We had a set back with the snorkeling trip to Gilligan鈥檚 island. We went into the surf shop to book a trip for the morning, and we were told that, the boat was being worked on, so there are no trips. This was fine, what are you going to do? The man also added, It wouldn鈥檛 have mattered anyway, you need a minimum of 6 passengers for them to make the trip. It just so happened that the resort was VERY secluded this particular week, (which I enjoyed). So we cut our losses woke up and rented a double kayak and paddled around all morning instead. When we returned we went up to our room, changed, and then went down to eat at the Las Palmas Cafe. While we were sitting there enjoying our lunch and drinking pina colada's we saw a couple walking out on the dock with snorkel gear. Then, a snorkel boat floated over from the other docks, picked up the TWO passengers and headed off, all this while we sat and watched infuriated at the scene, and of course we weren鈥檛 in our swimming gear so running out and stopping them wasn't an option. So they did take as little as two people on the boat, and obviously it wasn't broken. I went in the shop to figure out how this miscommunication could have happened, and of course the guy that fed us the line of B.S. wasn't working that day, and we were leaving the following morning.  So all in all the service is sub-par. A lot of the staff is friendly and a handful of them tend to look at you as a pain more than a customer. The resort is unbelievably beautiful. I have been to the Bahamas and Cancun, and this is as good or better in terms of quality landscaping. Nobody had written about the lack of services for the prices you pay to stay here, and that would have been a factor in my decision to stay here if I would have read that prior to booking this trip. Great getaway location, but the service needs an update.-RAJ, NH  
<Date>May 3, 2008

<Author>RNY
<Content>Beautiful Setting We rented a car in San Juan and drove to Copamarina. Just before Ponce we detoured to Tibes to see the very interesting native museum and reconstructed village. The guide was very knowledgeable. It's a challenge to find with few road signs but it's worth the effort and a visit. The resort is down a very narrow, twisty, hilly road. Once you finally get to the hotel the grounds are beautiful with manicured lawns and lots of flowers and Palm trees. The parking lot was full but the resort never felt crowded. There was enough room for everyone to spread out and find a quiet spot. The many beautiful pictures people have posted of the grounds are accurate. On the other hand, there are few pictures posted of the rooms which tend to be dark, small and rustic. We had an ocean front room in building three on the second floor with a balcony. Being an old resort the walls are not very thick so it's possible to hear conversations in the rooms on either side of you. There are vent windows over the shower in the bathroom that open onto the walkway and people should know their conversations in the bathroom can be heard by people passing by. Since we were on the second floor we didn't hear anyone walking above us but that might be a problem in the first floor rooms. The bathroom had obviously recently been renovated and was nicer than the one we had in San Juan with a big tiled shower. The room furniture could stand an updating. And as someone previously said the pillows were small, foam and not very comfortable. We used a back cushion from the chair as a pillow and that worked better.The balcony fan didn't work and two requests to have it fixed were ignored. The balcony furniture was stained and the privacy dividers were lattice so they gave little privacy. However, the view from the balcony was lovely. We ate dinner both nights at the Alexandra Restaurant. Usually we'd go off site after the first night but the resort is fairly isolated and the thought of driving the twisty road in the dark to return to the resort after dinner discouraged us. On the other hand, we had excellent meals both nights at the Alexandra. We ate one of the chef's seafood specials each night and each was delicious. They were of equal or better quality to the dinners we had in San Juan and of comparable cost. The buffet breakfast at Las Palmas was good with a cook making omelots and waffles but at $16 per person it was expensive for what each of us was able to eat. The pools were clean and beautiful and it was great that there were two adult pools, two kids pools, two whirlpools, as well as the beach. The water in the pools and at the beach was very warm which I really liked. The beach was very shallow which was fine for me but swimmers walked to the end of the long dock to find deeper water to swim in. We took the ferry to Gilligan's Island Saturday morning. The ferry and the island were very crowded. Even though only 200 people are allowed on the island each day it's a small island and it fills up quickly. It's a favorite daytrip for local extended families and they know the best places to go early to set up their grills, chairs. etc. There are no services on the island so you need to bring everything you'll need. The resort doesn't rent folding chairs but that would be very helpful since many of the areas have roots and stones which are not particularly comfortable for sitting. We snorkeled along some mangrove island roots and saw lots of Yellow Jacks. The current was very strong but we drifted with it so it worked out okay. All in all, the resort was pretty much what we expected as far as the rooms but the views, landscaping, and Alexandra's were better than we expected. Copamarina was a restful, quiet break from the hubbub of San Juan. I'm glad we decided to explore the south side of the island. It's a beautiful and peaceful area.  
<Date>Apr 23, 2008

<Author>BanannaDC
<Content>Great Resort - Wonderful Villa We spent a week in one of the villas at Copamarina, and really enjoyed it.The resort is small, but had everything we needed - a sandy beach, plenty of chairs and shady areas, several pools, water sports (kayaks, catamarans, snorkeling equipment, dive trips), and a beautiful setting for relaxing. The kids especially enjoyed the large grassy areas, the playground, and the inter tidal zone where they found many sea creatures. Outside of the resort we enjoyed hikes in the Guanica Dry Forest - the Copamarina offers a good trail guide.The spacious villa was great for us (6 adults  2 kids). There were 3 bedrooms and we set up 2 cots in one of the bedrooms to accommodate everyone. There was a complete kitchen, dining room, living room, 2 bathrooms, a wrap-around porch with ceiling fans, plus a washer and dryer. Being in the first floor villa, we were able to use the expansive grassy area as our own front yard. And to add my opinion to a couple previously addressed issues:1. Gilligan's Island - It was a nice boat ride and the snorkeling was fun. I would say it's good for first time or infrequent snorkelers, but if you've done nice reef snorkeling then you might find this disappointing. If you do go, be sure to snorkel all the way to where the river almost reaches the ocean, as that is where we saw most of the fish hiding among the mangrove roots. And that way you can swim back on the other fork of the river.2. Grassy Water - The water directly in front of the resort did have a lot of sea grass in it, but I didn't find that a problem. (It's just grass, right?) If you think you might be uncomfortable stepping in it, a pair of water shoes would be a good idea.The only small problems we had are listed below. They're quite minor, and would not stop us from returning.1. Ice machine in freezer not working, and no ice trays. We went to the ice machine in another building for ice.2. Bottom shelf on fridge door was missing, which limited storage space.3. Oven broiler tray missing, so we couldn't use the broiler.4. Not enough of some kitchen items (knives, small bowls, coffee cups).A wonderful trip, and we're all ready to go back!  
<Date>Apr 16, 2008

<Author>swimmom2mg
<Content>Overrated and overpriced We're at Copamarina now, and I must admit we're a bit disappointed. For the price, the service is less than what I would expect. In fact, the service (front desk, waiters in the restaurant) is quite impersonal. We arrived late last night, and even though our room is quite a ways from the restaurant, we could still hear the live music blaring in our room past 11. We had gone there for a drink right after arriving and the music was so loud, you could not even have a conversation. When I asked politely when the music would stop for the night, I was told 11pm (even though it was past 11 at the time) and there was nothing they could do. (How about asking them to turn down the volume a tad??!)Our kids are 14 and 12, and while they are finding ways to entertain themselves, there aren't a lot of other kids here their ages. Most of the kids are quite a bit younger.So far, the food (have just had one meal - the breakfast buffet - is just ok. Cost of the buffet was $16/each and they charge our 14 year old as an adult. Again, not worth it for the quality.We're going to eat in and around Guanica the rest of the trip, as much as possible. And while none of us are saying it, we are wishing we were back in Playa del Carmen at Shangri-La Caribe (where we went two years ago...they SO spoiled us!).I hope things turn around for the better, but right now I would not recommend Copamarina to my friends, especially for the price. It is a beautiful place though, just don't expect top notch service or a great beach (we knew about the beach before arriving).I am so hoping things get better. If they do, I will definitely post an update.P.S. Also, if you have any issues with pillows, be sure to bring your own. The ones here are very flat and foam...seem kind of old.

<Author>LotsaTraveling
<Content>Great Place to Relax and Escape Life's Hub bub We wanted to spend a week away and get some sun and relaxation without a lot of cost or multiple plane changes. Coming from NY, Puerto Rico seemed like a good option. So we checked out the Trip Advisor reviews, looked at the hotel prices and decided on the Copamarina Beach Resort. We were not disappointed. We flew from Newark into Aguadilla arriving after midnight and the drive to the resort was straightforward -- though you absolutely need a rental car. From the town of Guanica to the resort, you do have to drive along a narrow, windy road, so drive slowly and carefully especially at night. The resort was quiet, with excellent facilities. The pools and hot tubs were perfect for relaxation. And it was an easy drive to towns such as Ponce. We also spent a day going to El Yunque -- a fascinating spot but not an easy drive at all from Guanica -- I'd suggest saving it for a different trip (e.g., from San Juan or the Eastern shores of Puerto Rico).The hotel's restaurant is excellent, but we wanted to try other places as well. We enjoyed Rinc贸n Argentina in Ponce and Pito's Seafood, on Route 2, East of Ponce -- the service and food was excellent at both. The Blue Marlin in Guanica was fun and provided local color. There are plenty of fast food places around as well if you prefer that. The hotel staff were friendly and polite. The grounds were immaculately kept. They have a computer set up in a lounge for checking email. When it was down on one of the days, they let us use their office computer to print out our boarding passes.Some of the other reviews have commented on the beach. My step-daughter complained about sand flies at the beach but was quite content to sun herself by the pool. I went to Gilligan's Island and enjoyed the water, but didn't find it as impressive as the reviews would suggest. And the snorkeling was also unimpressive (lots of fish, but most were fairly drab). Apparently, they had to dock the boat in a different location because of hurricane damage so this may have accounted for the discrepancy in the reviews. The dry forest was interesting. The hotel distributes an excellent, illustrated brochure for those interested in hiking through it and seeing the botanical and animal life. The rooms were clean, comfortable and in typical Caribbean style. One night there was a family with multiple loud children in the adjoining room but they left the following day. We couldn't tell if the walls were thin or the sound was traveling through the door that connected our room to theirs. Or whether they were just extremely loud children. (But we think it was the latter.) I suspect they were less elegant than the rooms in the hotels on the East Coast; they were definitely less elegant that the rooms in the beach hotels where I've stayed in San Juan such as the Caribe Hilton. But our week's stay cost us about 1/3 of the price that we would have spent at any of those places for 3 travelers/2 rooms. Overall, the Copamarina was just what we wanted: a quiet, friendly, laid-back, relaxing spot to catch some rays and get a flavor for the area. We'd be quite happy to return at any time!  
<Date>Mar 28, 2008

<Author>seatofthepants
<Content>Beautiful grounds, terrible food The Copamarina grounds are beautiful, but the food at the cafe, which is the only restaurant within miles that serves breakfast or lunch, was horrific and expensive--especially considering the poor quality. Our main complaints were lack of freshness and low quality, which we found unforgiveable from such a luxurious ($$$) property . While our family of 4 (mom, dad, 22 year old and 12 year old) hails from the S.F. Bay Area and has high standards when it comes to food, we travel frequently and try to eat simple local food because it's the freshest and usually the most tasty. Unfortunately, nothing seemed fresh at the cafe. The warm fruit salad looked like it had been stewing in its own juice for quite a while and the shrimp in the casa dia had a decidedly over-the-hill odor. Even just a basic turkey sandwich was made with gelatinous pressed meat and served on squishy bread--hardly what one would expect at a high-end resort where most guests are at least somewhat health conscious. As much as we loved the property, we left after just two nights although we were scheduled to stay for five. Our stomachs was rumbling and our 12 year old was bouncing off the walls since she was pigging out on the only food she could stand: chips and ice cream from the snack shop.NOTE: We must add that the food at the Alexandra Restaurant, which only serves dinner, is very good. This establishment is formal and not appropriate for small children. It is also quite pricey. Plan on spending at least $200 for a family of 4.One last thing: there is grass growing in this bay and it is very shallow so unless you just want to get your feet wet in the ocean, plan on swimming in the pools.

<Author>AlliJo1980
<Content>Our Favorite Hotel in PR Of all the resorts we booked for our stay in Puerto Rico this was our favorite. We booked it to be semi-close to the bioluminescent bay in La Parguera (about 20 min) and were very impressed with the resort. Even though it is a little off the beaten path, I think that is part of what gives it its charm. We had a great room with a private terrace overlooking the water. The beach area was great with plenty of chairs, straw huts, etc. and a waiter circulating regularly for drinks, food, etc. We ate lunch at the outside bar/restaurant and found the food great and reasonably priced. We ate dinner at Alexandra's (the resort restaurant) after reading good reveiws about it. It was definitely good food, but of course higher prices than their outside restaurant/bar b/c it was finer dining - well worth it though! They also have a shop where they set up snorkeling/dive trips. We took a snorkeling trip from the hotel and had a great time! I would definitely recommend this resort.

<Author>mweez
<Content>Relaxation at its best When we viewed the pictures of the CopaMarina on their website it looked very relaxing. The pictures did not disappoint. The property is very well maintained and beautiful. My wife and I stayed at the resort for five nights and four days and enjoyed every minute of it. We did not find one cross or rude employee all of the resort staff was nice and eager to help (especially Raoul at the bar and Kris at the front desk). Raoul, my friend, always had a smile and would go out of his way to help you, also Kris at the front desk was helpful with all of our questions and offered many suggestions. Also the housekeepers did a fantastic job our room was spotless the whole stay.This is not a resort for travelers looking for nightlife and shopping. It is isolated and very relaxing, just what we wanted.The only negative is the isolation (as mentioned before in other reviews), it takes two hours from San Juan and at least 45 mins to get anywhere else. To sum it up, it was worth the 2 hr drive from San Juan. The food is great and the resort is wonderful. If you want a nice resort to relax to the waves, this is the one.

<Author>nova654
<Content>Hidden Jewel in Southwest Puerto Rico We have been to Puerto Rico many times since we have family there. We previously stayed in either Condado or Dorada area and wanted to stay on the southern side of the island for a change as we had never visited that part of the island.After doing some research on TripAdvisor, we decided to go try Guanica and the CopaMarina. There are not many resorts in the south. I originally wanted to stay in Ponce, but none of the hotels appealed to us (and after visiting the town, I am glad we did not stay there, although the city center is very charming).We did get a room far away from the restaurants in building 5, but once we were in the room, the walk to anything on the property took less than 2 minutes.The resort does not have that many rooms, but with 2 story buildings, it has quite a bit of property. It has 2 hot tubs, 2 children's pools and 2 big pools, although one is not deeper than 3 1/2 ft. Very family friendly although teenagers may get bored. Many families with babies through early teens.The beach was not ideal, although folks went to the end of the dock and were swimming past the seaweed. Although the public beach was a short walk, it had a yellow flag (no swimming) for the 6 days we were there. The one main area for improvement is the beach toys. There are a few non-motorized toys and they were broken for most of our stay.We had the all inclusive and while it was pricey for the area, it was a bargain if you are used to San Juan prices. (We spent almost $200 for dinner for 2 at Pikayo in San Juan, and while it was better quality, not sure it was $100 better). We found the service to be a little slow but we weren't in a rush. We did find the staff to be very friendly and any time we asked for something a little special, it was no problem...both in the outdoor cafe and Alexandra's. No request was denied.The resort was probably less than half full except for the weekend. It was one of the few resorts in PR that had a good number of locals staying there and many of them came only for the weekend. However, when we thought we would stay one extra night, the first person we asked at the desk said no problem and we could stay in the same room. We then had to be sure we could change our Condado reservation. Once we did, different people were at the front desk and they told us we couldn't stay in our room and no room of our category was available. Once we said the other person said we could, they just said ok. Not sure if they were trying to upsell us or what.Even with that front desk experience, we liked the relaxing atmosphere so much we stayed one extra night and will definitely go back!  
<Date>Mar 9, 2008

<Author>zendar
<Content>Scuba Divers Read This About Copamarina In Guanica Normally I don't make a habit of writing negative reviews. I simply felt obligated to put something on the internet to discourage other more experienced divers from making the same mistake that I unfortunately did.I do wreck diving in the deep and cold waters of New England year round and have gone diving all over the world. After reading about the amazing wall diving in Puerto Rico I decided to go there with my family on vacation. After 3 or 4 phone calls I booked a week long series of dives at Copamarina. I even called there the day before our trip to check if things were still OK.On the morning of our arrival I called the dive shop to see if the boat was going out that afternoon as planned. I was then told that the dive boat was broken and that there would be no diving all week. Suffice to say, I was devastated. I asked if they could help me to find another boat. They were extremely unhelpful and hung up the phone on me even though I was not being rude or impolite about the situation ( I would prefer to think that we were disconnected by accident, but I am not sure that was true). I explained that I had spent a lot of money to come to Copamarina and that I had made all my vacation plans on the assumption that they were a world class diving resort with regularly scheduled boat trips. I was then told that the real reason the boat was broken was that they didn't have a minimum of 3 people to go, and that this was true for the entire week.. Base on other people's similar accounts on this web site, it seems like the boat is broken with astonishing regularity. Is there some reason why they couldn't be honest and tell me this ahead of time so I could have made plans to go elsewhere in Puerto Rico?? Instead I found myself trapped in a less than optimal situation.I called the manager 3 times and spoke to people who said that he/she would call me right back, but no one ever did. Funny how the management seem so fastidious about replying to negative feedback on the internet, but they don't want to deal with customers who are genuinely upset.Ultimately I went to Parguera 20 miles away and dove with Paradise Dive Shop and West Divers both of whom were excellent. The wall diving was extremely impressive and worth the trip. Just for the record, Parguera divers is no longer operating even though they are still listed on the internet as a dive charter in the same area.The real problem is that the management of the Copamarina should stop falsely advertising that they are a world class dive resort comparable to other such resorts. Its simply not true. It is sad that no one in the hotel administration seems to have any sense of vision. They are sitting on one of the best places to dive in the Carribean, but they do not seem to support the dive shop adequately enough to truly make it a world class diving destination like the Caymans or Aruba. They easily could attract many more divers if they simply got their act togetherAs far as the Copamarina resort itself , I have no complaints. The grounds were beautiful, the service was excellent and the food was well prepared.The local economy would greatly benefit if they really tried to develop their natural diving resources. This would also have a trickle down effect on the amount of business in the other dive shops in the area. Maybe they should talk to each other and get better organized. It would be a win/ win situation for all.SO BEWARE. UNTIL THEY GET THEIR ACT TOGETHER I WOULD GO ELSEWHERE TO DIVE OR BE PREPARED FOR A GREAT DISAPPOINTMENT.  
<Date>Feb 27, 2008

<Content>Always Relaxing This is my fourth stay at the Copa in two years. Heretofore, I've always stayed in oceanfront accomodations. <Author>janbsn
<Content>Copamarina just okay My husband and I stayed here for 4 nights in an ocean view room for $285/nt. The room wasn't anything special, and the lighting is terrible, but it was clean. I agree with a previous review where they stated this is a 3-star trying to be a 5-star. I would definitely not take their all-inclusive (we didn't) as the food is not that good and there are places you can drive to, if you like to search out local restaurants. Most everyone in the area speaks some English - and with our very limited Spanish we never had a problem in this part of PR. We found a breakfast place (panderia) down the hill from here (on the main st in Guanica village area - which is behind McDonald's off Rte 116) and had either fried eggs or an omelet with coffee and toast for about $7 for the two of us, compared to the Copamarina's breakfast buffet for about $40 and their $42 lunch for a sandwich/soft drink each. If you're squeamish about driving windy, hilly roads, don't go to the Copamarina - it's a very steep, narrow, curvy road for about 3 miles. The beach is full of sea grass - you can wade out to about mid-calf, and then you're in that slimy grass. We did go off the end of the boat pier where there is a ladder into the water, but it's only sandy just at the bottom of the ladder - the sea grass and muck is out there too. We weren't able to go over to Gilligan's Island because of previous storm damage, but they did take us out to another beach around a point via boat for $6 each. The people who went on the diving boat had to be towed back 6-7 mi, so I get the feeling that everything is not taken care of as it should be. I would look for another place before returning to the Copamarina.  
<Date>Jan 23, 2008

<Author>heart&sole
<Content>Didn't want to leave My wife 3 yo daugther and I spent 5 blissful days at Copamarina starting on January 5th. We booked a deluxe ocean front room. Which was clean. Many of the other rooms on the property have partial ocean views so those wishing to save some money can book garden view rooms without missing out. We took the all inclusive meal plan based on the online menu and the fact that the hotel would happily provide box lunches. This way we could take our lunch and explore the puerta del sol. We had dinner each night in their restaurant Alexandra which was very good most nights and fantastic on 2 occasions! Service was always professional and the staff was only too happy to accommodate special requests. Lunch was usually a nice fresh grilled piece of fish with veggies at Las Palmas. The grounds are immaculate, the beach cleaned every morning and we found the staff helpful and quite friendly. We purposely traveled the week after Christmas break and were rewarded to find the resort uncrowded. Local families and others from the States made up the majority of visitors. Most local families were curious to know how we found out about this place since its off the beaten path which adds to the specialness of Copamarina. Yes the resort is about 2 hours from San Juan but thats the reward. For those with long flights into San Juan, you may want to consider spending a night or two in San Juan before heading South. The resort has 5 pools, two infant and 3 regular. BTW lunch can be delivered poolside!! We spent a good deal of time in the pools so the issues of sea grass in the ocean didn't bother us. There is a staircase into the water at the end of the dock so if you want to swim beyond the seagrass, you can. We played on the beach and took the hobie cat out sailing everyday. The price of which is included in the all inclusive package.One highlight was the day 5 dolphins swam with us as we sailed to guiligans Island. Overall, we had a wonderful time and Copamarina is the type of resort that you can actively travel the local area or just hang out on the beach. Our only disappointment was the bedroom pillows. For the price, we would have expected plush pillows. Instead, the ones in our room were hard and lumpy. Would we go back? We didn't want to leave. Next time maybe we'll bring our own pillows!  
<Date>Jan 18, 2008

<Author>RBandJB
<Content>Very relaxing resort Copamarina Beach ResortDecember 25, 2007-January 1, 2008Trip Advisor member from NE ColoradoThis is a very quiet place for families and those wanting a relaxing vacation. The food was very good and the staff very professional and helpful. Rooms were clean and maid service was excellent.We did rent a car, so we left the resort and went to some nearby beaches and sites. These were spots the people from Puerto Rico enjoyed and all were clean and quiet. Everything was closed down around sundown in the fenced parks. We enjoyed the local eateries and the local towns. The people in the towns were friendly and helpful. We attended a softball game and looked forward to seeing the young boys of the towns ride their horses in the evenings. Our trips to the nearby lighthouses, salt flats, and surfing areas were interesting also. Our journeys into the mountains were on winding and narrow roads, but a good picture of the lifestyle of the citizens of the island. I would recommend this resort to anyone. It was a good vacation and even though we do not speak Spanish, we could understand the road signs and take care of the basics.

<Author>Richard2Phila
<Content>Great place to relax Recent stay with two teenage boys at CopaMarina was a pleasure. Beautiful view from all hotel rooms.Gilligans Island for snorkeling was closed due to dock being out from recent storm--so went to alternate site--just 10 minute boat ride. Previous Trip Advisor reviews discussed the fact that CopaMarina's on site dive shop was not well run--but our experience was very good -- the divemaster appeared to be in his late 30's and he has been there for two years. Alternate dive shops are located in Paraquera-about 30 minutes away. They include Paradise Scuba [--], Parquera Divers and Boqueron Dive shop.In order to avoid any cabin fever we did use our car to drive to Parquera for excellent meal at La Casita--highly recommend it.Very popular with those that know the area.Also drove 30 minutes back towards Ponce to eat on the ocean at Pitos reataurant--right on Rt 712. Very scenic setting but some noise from highway.

<Author>86hoya
<Content>Good choice, from a parent's perspective Spent five days at Copamarina the week after Thanksgiving, with a two year old and a four year old. Property was only 1/3rd full, so if you go during the busy season (Christmas-Easter, and then again June and July), you may have a different experience. The resort is a 2 1/2 hour drive from the San Juan airport - all highway (toll roads) with plenty of places to stop along the way for pitstops, snacks. Unlike the US you dont get much notice about upcoming exits/food/fuel, so be ready to get off the highway at a moments notice. From the town of Guanica, the resort is 10 minutes on a narrow road that follows the coast. Guanica has a McDonalds, Burger King, mid sized grocery store, health clinical/pharmacy, but not much else - if you run out of diapers etc, you can easily get it there.Food - we were on the all inclusive plan, but you ordered off the same menu as the non AI guests. Breakfast service started at 7am...dinner at the out-door cafe started at 630, and the more formal indoor restaurant at 6pm. Menus were varied and large enough that you wouldnt have to re-order if you stayed less than a week. Children's menu was available - pizza, hot dogs, grilled cheese, smaller portions of other entries as well. The staff was very flexible on allowing substitutes - could take french fries off and add brocoli, fruit etc to any menu item. Activities - five pools, two of which were knee deep and just for little kids, and a 3rd pool (main) that had a shallow area/section. Jungle gym/play area was located right off the outdoor cafe. Beach area wasnt very big, but water was very calm. As others mention, water was grassy and not that clear, but very child friendly in terms of access and safety. They had a tennis court but didnt see anybody using it, a spa and an indoor workout facility, plus a game room.TV - roughly 20 channels, most in English, including multiple HBO and Disney options, but strangely enough no ABC, CBS or NBC. Evening activity - not much. Aside from the solo-guitarist who played each night in the cafe, this was a very quiet hotel. If you are looking for dancing, gambling etc, you are in the wrong spot. If you are looking for a calm quiet family place - go for it.Computer - only downside to the hotel was that it offered wireless in the room, but we werent able to connect - we were in building 5, the furthest from the main building. There was one desktop with internet acess (free) and we never had a problem getting on...but again, the hotel was lightly booked.Overall a good place to go with small children as long as you want a laid back vacation.  
<Date>Dec 7, 2007

<Author>AZkim
<Content>The highlight of our Puerto Rico vacation I typically only write reviews when something happens on a vacation that left me feeling extremely dissatisfied. This time, I am writing a review for the exact OPPOSITE reason. I have never had a MORE satisfying experience.First of all, I would like to thank the staff of the Copamarina Resort for making sure my family and I had an incredble stay. Immediately, upon check in, I could tell this resort was there to please it's customers. We arrived a few hours before check in and I was feeling car sick. I was feeling quite cranky and unhappy......for about 30 seconds after arriving at the Copamarina. The staff could tell I was not feeling well and allowed us to check in early. They even allowed us to preview our suite and pick out which one suited us. We chose to upgrade to a very nice two room suite so my husband and I could enjoy some privacy. After being there a day, we realized that it would have been a better financial move for us if we would have purchased the all inclusive package. After having a casual conversation with one of the staff members about types of drinks she suggested, I jokingly mentioned to her about drinking away my kids' college fund. She suggested that we go all inclusive and promptly returned with the manager. He reviewed our charges and said that it would be to our benefit if we converted......even allowed it to be retroactive....which saved us a substantial amount of money. It cost our family of four 150.00 per day for the all inclusive plan. That's typically what we would spend on just dinner and drinks. I was so impressed that they allowed us to do that!! That they would consider our wallet before their own.The grounds were beautiful. The pools were very clean with a spectacular carribean view. The food was great.....and the drinks were even better!! I tried everything they suggested....the bartenders were superb!We stayed at 3 resorts all over the island. We had a good experience at all the resorts we stayed at, but Copamarina was the best. The reason being because of the incredibly attentive staff seeing to it that we had a GREAT stay. We are planning on returning next year.....this time, all 10 days will be spent at this resort!!

<Author>Robert90
<Content>Very pleasant stay at the Copamarina My wife, teenage son  I just returned from a 3 night stay at the Copamarina and were very please with our experience. The resort is very well maintained and staffed by pleasant and helpful people. We arrived well before check in time due to our flight and were given a room to relax in until our scheduled room was ready.  I recommend this location to people who wish a more quiet and peaceful vacation in a great location. There are plenty of things to do such as diving, fishing  boating to a local mangrove island with a small beach. The resort is located next to the dry forest reserve and there are great walking trails along the ocean with hidden beaches and great views. In addition, this part of Puerto Rico receives little rain annually, so you can count on excellent weather.  Swimming is not great as the water is shallow at the resort beach, but this is not a problem as there are many opportunities for good swimming and snorkeling nearby.  This is not the spot for fans of loud mega resorts and casinos. If you go ask Ruben to take you in the boat to snorkeling spots. He works hard to make sure you have a good time.

<Author>edepoix
<Content>Beautiful and relaxing honeymoon We just got back from our honeymoon in Puerto Rico. We stayed 3 nights at the Copamarina, and 3 nights in Old San Juan. We absolutely LOVED the Copamarina. There were a few downsides, but I think the reason we loved it was because those downsides weren't particularly disturbing to us. Our first impression was the open-air lobby, which is very pretty, with orchids planted in the palm trees. The staff at the front desk was very nice, professional, and helpful. They upgraded our room when they heard we were on our honeymoon. Our room was very nice...large and clean. It wasn't overly luxurious, but definitely nice. The first night, we spent several hours enjoying the open-air bar/cafe (there are two restaurants: the cafe/bar, which is a casual menu, and Alexandra, which is fancier. ) The bartender was awesome (all the bartenders who served us during our stay were super attentive and friendly.) The drinks were great. We ordered some food off the cafe menu, and it was mediocre. We were so happy to be relaxing with drinks with a view of the Caribbean Sea, that we didn't care too much. Breakfast was great - the menu is pretty good: eggs benedict, etc. We took a sea kayak to Gilligan's Island, which is absolutely gorgeous (the highlight of the entire trip). I guess October is right in the middle of the off season, so there was no one there (very few people at the resort in general, which was great). Anyway, we kayaked around a cluster of islands, and swam on another deserted beach called Bellena Beach. Dinner at Alexandra that night was great. It wasn't the best thing I'd ever eaten in my life, but definitely better than the cafe. I liked the food. I thought the filet mignon was good. My husband got the Mofongo, which he liked. The second day we hiked in the Dry Forest, which is slightly overrated, but still interesting and a good little workout. Each night we relaxed in the hot tub, which was nice. We also enjoyed the pool nearest our room, and a few hours on the beach in recliners.As I mentioned in the beginning, there were a few possible downsides:- other posters are right - as far as night time entertainment. It's basically a guy playing guitar at the bar. We loved it. We weren't there to go clubbing, we were there to have some drinks, and enjoy each other's company. - Cafe food isn't great. But we liked the other restaurant.- other posters are right, the beach isn't good. We didn't care, though, because we live near the beach in the States, so we didn't feel disappointed. If you're looking for a really beachy time, you shouldn't go there. Their beach is short, and the bottom is mucky and there are lots of underwater plants. Gilligans Island is great though. That's all the bad parts. What we loved: the beautifully maintained grounds, deserted pools and hot tubs, Gilligan's Island, GREAT service without exception, awesome outside bar, nice room. We hope to go back.  
<Date>Oct 22, 2007

<Author>skw3
<Content>beautiful grounds, hospitality lacking I have to admit I had high expectations after reading all the glowing reviews but the Copamarina is not all that. You have to pay in advance to stay here and it is billed as a resort so I expected wait staff to be of good quality and speak english well.We stayed immediately after hurricane Dean passed by the island with essentially no damage to PR. As we drove up we noted a very strong dead fish odor. When I asked the staff it it was due to the hurricane I got no answer. The front desk staff was efficient but not welcoming at all. We had already stayed at the Melia in Ponce and the Hilton Caribe in San Juan and had been warmly greetedat both of those hotels. The beach was full of seaweed and tons of debris washed in by the tide and they were literally bulldozing it away. This process went on the entire 3 days we were there and the beach was completely unuseable the entire time. I know this could not be helped but it would have made us feel a lot better if one staff member had acknowledged it. The room was very clean and well maintained as was all the grounds. They were constantly busy cutting bushes, grass, etc. It seemed that everything was spotless except our patio which was covered with leaves and twigs. Also, the children's waiting pools were full of leaves. I called the front desk and asked if someone would sweep as wewere tracking a lot of dirt inside but noone ever came. I finally asked the maid who was cleaning the room (she was the only employee who talked to us personally our entire stay and was quite pleasant). If you stay here you are not near other hotels or a town with restaurants so be prepared to eat at their 2 restaurants. The first evening we went to Las Palmas and the service was impersonal but efficient and everything was fine. We planned on eating in the Alexandra the next. We spent the next morning swimming at the pool (skipped breakfast-we're not big eaters) and opted for lunch at Las Palmas. This ended up being the worst service I think I can ever remember at a restaurant. We have traveled through the states and europe so I am well aware of levels of service. Let me explain, this is an open air restaurant, you walk up and pick where you want to sit. A male waiter acknowledged us and we sat down. From this point on I had to flag him for everything. First for menus which he brings 2 of and there are 3 of us. I politely ask for a third.I flag for water, he brings bottles. I say thanks but tap water is fine. The glasses of tap water sit on the bar forever and I think maybe I should just go get them but he is standing near the bar disinterested in anything through all of this. Flag to order. He says your waitress is Maria. OK so I guess I'm supposed to know this somehow? Apparently we were imposing on him because he clearly did not want to do anything. Maria shows up with the food! I am still calm at this point, and she asks do I want condiments with my ($10) hamburger? Yes, please. Well, the hamburger is pretty dry and so I figure I'll wait until they come- and wait, and wait. They come-the tough parts of a few pieces of some iceberg lettuce and a slice of hard,yellow tomato. Could I have some mustard or mayonaise? Here she looks at me like she has never heard of these. These come-in large gravy pitchers! At this point she wants to know if everything is ok. At tell her no but only zero in on the no service earlier. She says that some people here do not do teamwork. Do I want to speak to the manger? Sure, maybe they can fix things. No manager shows up, no waitress after that, and no ticket. I finally just got up and left with my son, 20 and daughter, 15. Believe me they would have let me know if mom was being rude. There were 4 table eating and more wait staff than that was just standing around. I got the distinct feeling they were in their off season and really didn't care. That night wewent into Yauco several miles east and had some some delicious Subway sandwiches, excellent service, the man behind the counter pleasantly joked with us and it cost $15. The front desk receptionist never asked me how our stay was when we checked out.. In fact he was busy answering phone calls even though there was another clerk behind the desk. Lastly, there are two nice but shallow pools. There was no pool service, if you want food or drink you will need to hoof it to the bar across the grounds.

<Author>MaishChicago
<Content>Great Place to Relax We took our family for a week for our first time in Puerto Rico. The resort is clean and well-equipped, the rooms comfortable although not luxurious, and the staff genuine and friendly. The pools areas and grounds are especially nice. We really enjoyed Irving's (the activities coordinator) Cave Hike. We recommend it for anyone reasonably fit - wear tennis/hiking shoes and consider taking a bandanna or damp rag as it can get a little messy inside the cave. Look for the GIANT Toad! The bar and live music was far above average - the Pina Coladas the Best! The food in the cafe/bar is alright, though much better in the restaurant Alexanders. Buffet Breakfast was more than generous - buy it with your package if possible.Be prepared to need a little patience on excursions - the public ferry may not be on time, as it fills up and may need to come back for you on another trip. The snorkeling was worth the money - good reef and helpful guides.Overall, it was a good value for your money, especially so in off season(summer months).

<Author>theasmo
<Content>Quiet and Relaxing Like many others here I first read many of these reviews prior to booking my vacation. The quantity of positive reviews here was actually pretty amazing, I almost wondered if this was too good to be true. Perhaps lots of relatives of employees were posting away!Well, I am happy to report that every positive review here is dead on. This resort is wonderful to stay at and is staffed with individuals of the highest caliber. I was amazed by the common concern that all staff members shared for the comfort of their guests. The maintenance and gardening crew, front desk, waiters and bartenders, cooks, pool and beach crew, store staff, etc... Everyone was so polite and helpful, and when needed were always willing to go above and beyond to ensure your visit was perfect.The resort was very clean and the grounds crew was out every day ensuring it stayed that way. The pool was cleaned every morning, I woke up early enough every day to see them doing so. The rooms were spacious, clean, and most certainly set the mood for relaxation.I booked a 4 night all inclusive. This was well worth the cost for me as I am a bit of a drinker and I love to eat! We were here for the first week of August, just after the local children were back in school. So the resort was very quiet, although it was still fully staffed! This time is considered part of their off season, however it was still a wonderful experience.The food was good at the outside cafe and very good for the inside fine dining. I was so conerned about the bar closing around 11:30pm and thought I would be left wanting a drink after, however I was so busy during the day that I never made it past 10:30pm any given night! This is good as there is no local night life. So if you're looking to have a busy day, a few drinks by the pool, and a good dinner and some relaxing music, then this is a place for you. If you're looking to go clubbing at night, then you need to look elsewhere. My only disappointment with the resort, and this is just personal preference, would be the beach. I enjoy a rough surf and diving into waves. The sea here is like a bathtub, very little movement and pretty warm. Obviously this will appeal to many, but may not for those used to a little action in the water.I am already planning my next trip back, and so I recommend this resort to anyone looking to get away for relaxation. From others I have met there I understand that it is much busier and less quiet during their regular season, so I plan on doing another offseason trip. I want to end by thanking the Copamarina staff for ensuring our vacation was wonderful, they really are great people there!!

<Author>MrGelhs204
<Content>Hidden Gem Copamarina was exactly what our family was looking for: a relaxed, well maintained, comfortable, out of the way resort with outstanding service. We booked the package with breakfast buffet included - it was outstanding. We went out for lunch and dinner at various local places in the area and I recommend you do the same. We did not use the resort restaurants for lunch/dinner, but generally heard positive comments. It seemed some of the service issues that folks have mentioned here had been corrected. Rooms are spacious, clean, and well appointed. There is live music every night at the bar, but don't go there expecting any kind of nightlife. This is a place to rest and relax. Don't miss the trip to Gilligan's Island. You are picked up right at Copamarina's dock - very short ride to Gilligans. We swam in the mangrove all the way to the ocean - safe - no point is more than 5 feet deep. Copamarina offers dive tours but we did not take advantage of it. Car is a must if you want to see other great beaches in the area - the one at copamarina is not exactly the best. All of the pools at Copa, the gym, and tennis courts are quality. The staff is attentive and nice in a natural way. Lots of families, excellent service (sometimes a tough find in PR),

<Author>lucayan
<Content>Nice time.Lovely resort. Copamarina is a lovely resort. The staff were friendly and helpful. The sea was warm. The breakfasts at the Las Palmas restaurant were plentiful and well planned. The room was clean and spacious. Alexandre's (indoor and classy) is a fine but pricey restaurant. We (myself, wife and 14-year-old son) really enjoyed our time here. He did his first scuba dive. Great fun, and very professional service. We saw some nice reef fish, though not quite in the profusion of some Caribbean destinations. The vast majority of guests are local, and this is reflected in the atmosphere, which is lively and gregarious. If you want to eat outside the resort, be aware that Puerto Rican cuisine does not sit at the top of Latin American culinary style, and that the local offerings are sparse. Gilligan's Island is often crowded, but the snorkelling is good. You really need a rental car to see anything else...do drive to San Juan (a couple of hours, but worth it) for the architecture and history. Just up the road from the resort are some outstanding beaches. Guanica (the nearest town) is not tourist oriented, but the dockfront really rocks for locals on weekends. This end of the island isn't really built for tourists, but in many ways that's OK. Oh, and last but not least, if you're noise sensitive, some of the rooms may keep you awake. Overall, I'm happy we went. So too will you be, I think.  
<Date>Jul 28, 2007

<Author>Cpuhog
<Content>Liked the place ...but Alexandra's service was BAD and beach is no good I am from PR but have lived in the states for 10+ years. This summer we decided to visit my island and stay in a local resort. CopaMarina looked great ... loved the room and the overall presence of care takers. The pools were clean and in great great shape. The beach is not good for anything but to walk and walk. It is toooooo shallow and coverd with marine plants almost in its entirety. So, the highlights are the pool and the room. There is no room service and the food in the Palma's Cafe is not that great with the exception of the breakfast buffet. However, their service at the Cafe is great...too bad the food is not as described in the menu (e.g. teriyaki wings with little to NO teriyaki sauce, fish fillets that actually fish sticks, the Parcha sauce with little to NO Parcha (passion fruit) flavor) ... Now in our last night we decided to eat dinner at Alexandra's (their good restaurant). We understand that service has ups and downs but we were lucky enough to receive the WORST service ever during our dinner. We made reservations for 8pm as requested by their staff. We arrived and were taken to our table then we were told that Jonathan was our waiter ... no no it is Lorenzo ... but Lorenzo did NOT stopped at our table ever during the night. Around 20 minutes passed and the head-waiter noticed our long faces (I know we could have said something but for some time we were engaged in conversation) .. he stopped asking for our order...but we had not even been asked for our drinks ... ok, he took our drinks (no alcohol that night) and our dinner order...... waited ... waited.... people came in .. got to their tables ..ordered ..got their food.... 45minutes later we got ours. I noticed Lorenzo dancing around the tables serving others but never stopped by. Other waiters topped water glasses around ... not in our table ...my son ran out of soda .. nobody asked to get a new one until we stopped one of them ... nobody stopped and checked on our experience ... The food was bland in flavor (little seasoning on the fillet mignon) and in the case of my mofondo-de-camarones (mashed plantains with shrimp inside) the shrimps were not removed entirely from their shell which made eating the mix a stop-n-go affair.We had to stop them and ask for the check ... we left ... NO TIP.I love my island .. but one thing that is true is the spottiness (is that a word?) of the customer service. I hope you have a better experience than I did at CopaMarina. The grounds are beautiful ... the rooms are big and clean ... the pools are very very nice.

<Author>BfromSC
<Content>Beautiful Resort but Scuba Diving Not Available - DIVERS READ! We just returned from a nice visit to the Copamarina last week. The grounds are beautiful, room was nice, and overall we had a good time. The main issue we had was that scuba diving was not available all week. When we checked in on Tuesday we were told that there would not be any diving available until Saturday, the day we were flying back to the US. The hotel employee was very nice and said that May is a slow month so the scuba employees decided to take a job all week repairing a reef that had been badly damaged. She said that we could go diving through a different dive shop that is 30 minutes away. She did not say anything good about the shop, but simply said they do diving. We would have to drive there or they could call us a cab. My husband and I do not dive very often so we always research dive shops before we go diving with them. We had already researched the Copamarina and felt very confident that this is a solid dive shop with a good reputation, however we did not know anything about the dive shop that is 30 minutes away. We did not bring our laptop and the Copamarnia does not have any available computers, so we did not have a way to do any online research. Therefore we decided not to go diving. I guess we could have driven the 30 minutes and tried to find out more about the dive shop, but we had been stuck in horrible traffic in San Juan for 3 hours and simply did not want to get back in the car. We came there expecting to dive onsite, not have to drive 30 minutes to a dive shop that may or may not be reputable. If you are not a diver, I would recommend you stay at the Copamarina because it is very nice and peaceful. We did not do the all inclusive meal plan, but I might consider it if we go back because there are not too many places nearby to eat. I thought the food was good and we enjoyed the open air cafe and the music at night. The only other issue we had is that you can hear everything in the room next door through the connecting locked door. The first night we woke up at midnight because the people were talking and when they sneezed at 6:00 am it was so loud I thought someone was in our room. I complained and was moved to a room that had a vacant room next door. However, during high season this might not be possible. The doors are very thin and need some insulation. I guess the bottom line is that if you are a diver and plan to dive, I would not stay there. Our experience is not isolated if you read the other reviews it happened to another reviewer in March of this year. However, if you are simply wanting a nice vacation in relaxing area then the Copamarina is a good choice. Feel free to email me with questions.
