<Author>JQ_Citizen
<Content>Well above average Private beach which was surprisingly uncrowded considering the number of rooms at this resort. Staff unfailingly courteous with, at a minimum, a working knowledge of English. Rooms clean, modern, comfortable, with a small patio. Guanica is a very dry area but the resort grounds had plenty of greenery and large palm trees. Wireless internet access extended to rooms. 2 pools, 2 hot tubs, Hobie, kayak, and other water rentals available.Breakfast at Las Palmas Cafe is buffet style and excellent, with made-to-order egg ishes and a wide selection of food. Lunch and dinner menu limited and nothing special; all meals at the cafe are reasonably priced. The onsite dinner restaurant was very good with a good wine selection, and a bit expensive.Not a whole lot to do in this section of the country, but PR is a small island so it's easy to drive to Ponce or other towns for some history  culture. If you intend to stay resort-bound, you'll be very happy with the Copamarina.Overall, good value for the money and very positive experience.

<Author>BigDog67
<Content>Great Family Vacation! My family just returned from a week at the Copamarina. This is the first time I am writing a review on trip advisor, largely because I chose the property based on trip advisor reviews. I hope this is helpful. Also, I travel a lot for business and have stayed at many outstanding resorts, so I think I'm a pretty good judge of things.The Copamarina was a great choice for us -- my wife, 10 year-old son, and 6 year-old daughter. It is a beautiful property with grounds that are immaculately maintained and located in a visually stunning part of Puerto Rico. We have stayed on more exotic islands and this area in SW PR rivaled many of those places. We are an active family. My kids are outstanding swimmers and athletes, and we were active the entire time with great activities. Obviously, with young children, their enjoyment largely dictates the quality of the vacation. They never wanted to leave the resort! We did not do the all-inclusive, though next time we will. The area around the hotel, after the beautiful forest ends, is largely poor and there are not many good restaurants. The food at the property restaurants was good, and sometimes very good, but not great. But certainly much better than anything else around. How good? One night, the former Governor of PR sat at the table next to us. I assume that means its OK!Part of what makes this place great are the people that work there. The staff( Wilmer, Irving, JJ, Lisbeth, Rosa, etc.) are amazing and made us and our kids feel totally at home. Meet these people and befreind them -- they added so much to our experience! The activities are something off of the Discovery Channel. The pools are beautiful and inviting. Also, of major importance to us, the beach stays very shallow for like 50 yards out, which is a total stress releiver when traveling with a 6 year old. A lot of how much you like a vacation is about expectations. So to level set yours about the Copamarina -- it is not a super luxury hotel in any sense of the word. It's funny -- I almost don't want to say too much and make this place too popular! But I want to be honest, because trip advisor helped us out. If you're looking for a Four Seasons experience, you will be disappointed. There was a couple there who were bemoaning that it wasn't nearly as nice as Fiji or Hawaii. Duh, it's Puerto Rico! But if you are an easy going family looking for a fun week in a beautiful caribean resort, you'll dig this place.

<Content>perfect! My teenage daughter and i just returned from our annual spring break trip. We Stayed 7 days at the Copamarina and loved every minute of it. It is wonderfully relaxing and we felt safe the entire time.We rented a car in San Juan and drove to the resort. There were no troubles at all. The breakfast and lunch menus were really good, too. The whole resort was very clean - there were constantly people picking up things and just tending to the grounds. <Author>ChiGirly
<Content>Please read if you have concerns about this resort We just got back from spending 8 days at the Copamarina and we had a wonderful time. We booked the trip through our Royal Holiday Club membership and I read everything there was on the web to read before our trip. I had some concerns about some of the things I read and I am happy to report that none of them were issues for my family. I have a 9 year old son and a 7 year old son and they had a blast. We flew into San Juan from Washington DC on a Tuesday night and practically had the whole plane to ourselves. We arrived at the San Juan airport around 10:30 p.m. and made the short walk with our luggage to the airport hotel and stayed the night (they have a small casino there if you like to gamble). The next morning we took the airport shuttle to Hertz and picked up our rental car. If you rent a car, I strongly suggest spending the extra money and getting the GPS system. The Hertz system took us right to the resort without any difficulty. I spoke to others at the resort who got lost with poor directions they had obtained. We had a very pleasant drive to the resort even though I was a little concerned about everything I had read about Puerto Rican drivers. I will tell you that they do drive fast and they do not use their turn signals and will cut in front of you if you are not going fast enough so you just have to pay attention and move out of the way. Also, if you take the main highways to the resort from San Juan, make sure you have plenty of toll money with you. You will hit a few toll booths going to the resort (some tolls are high like $2.00鈥thers are .50) and you will hit several coming back. The road gets narrow once you get into Guanica and head up the hill towards the resort. There is enough roomfor two cars to pass and the road is paved but you need to go slowly around the corners and don鈥檛 rush. The resort is beautiful and the rooms are very tropical looking and clean. Our room had two queen beds, a mini frige and a very nice balcony overlooking the pool at the end of the resort. They have kid鈥檚 activities during the day (check at the front desk for the activity list and times) and J.J. is awesome with the children. My kids played soccer, twister, baseball, sack races, kayak races鈥nd the dive shop will usually give them prizes. My boys got t-shirts, bags, hats, stickers and tattoos. Unlike what other people said in their posts, I saw the security guards almost everyday we were there. I spoke to the one gentleman a couple of times and he was very good at making sure people weren鈥檛 coming down from the public beach and making sure there were no issues. The food is fantastic and I am very happy we did the all-inclusive. It cost $270 a day for all 4 of us and betweenthe fruity drinks, the kids eating little meals throughout the day, and our big lobster and steak dinners, the all-inclusive was the only way to go. One couple we met did not do the all inclusive and the one dinner they had on the resort was over $200 for the 4 of thembut they raved at how great the food was and that they should have paid for all inclusive and ate there every night instead of leaving the resort. Plus my children were in the kayaks and paddle boats a lot and that was included in the price also. We went to Gilligan鈥檚 Island but found that a little disappointing. The beaches there are not what you would think they would be and it is tuff to find a secluded spot if the island is crowded but we did see some beautiful fish so if you are going there, snorkeling is a must. We also did a hike in the Guanica Dry forest and went on a tour with Copamarina down into a cave that is not advertised to general public. It is a little steep getting in the cave and you will get dirty so make sure not to wear light colored clothes or anything you would not want to get dirty. My boys had a blast in the cave and really enjoyed it. Check at the front desk if you want to do it. It is just a short drive down the road from the resort. In general, the staff were great, the waiters and bar tenders are awesome, food is fantastic, it is very safe (I left my personal belongings at the pool every day and no one ever touched anything), we made a lot of new friends, the boys had a blast and it was just a very wonderful and memorable trip.The resort is quiet and not real rowdy and I could just let my children run the resort and I didn鈥檛 have to worry about them like I did when we were in Jamaica. The sun is very very intense though so if you have fair skin, I suggest getting zinc to keep on noses and ears. Also, the main bar closes around 11p.m. (but they did stay open late one night for us) and the smaller bar near the pool atthe far end of the resort closes at 5:00. Also, many of the local area attractions are closed on Mondays (and some on Tuesdays) so makesure you check before you head out somewhere. If you are lookingfor a nice quiet vacation or quality family time with the children, Copamarina is perfect!

<Author>AidanSineadsMom
<Content>Enjoyed the Copamarina We just returned from a stay in Puerto Rico that included the Copamarina. We found it beautiful and relaxing. I had read the earlier reviews and was not put off by most of the comments about the remoteness or lack of nightlife. We did not use the all-inclusive plan as we just couldn't contemplate eating that much food or using that many water toys. We had the junior suite, which included a refrigerator and microwage, so we usually ate one meal a day in the hotel restaurant and the others in the suite from groceries purchased in nearby Guanica. Staff is friendly and helpful. We took the boat to Gilligan's island and had fun snorkeling there. The hotel's beach is very shallow and calm, more like a wading experience. However, many of the kids were jumping off the pier, where it was deeper. A better swimming experience can be found at Cana Gorda, the public beach which is literally right next door to the hotel property and was almost deserted every day we were there. The pools are nice, with the pool furthest from the lobby tending to be more quiet.

<Author>get-out-of-the-cold
<Content>Copamarnia - Clean, Quiet and Relaxing The other reviews of Copamarina tell the story very well. We stayed there in the end of March and it met our expectations based on other reviews I read on Trip Advisor. A couple of points I will add:We did not do the all inclusive package and I was worried that there would be no place for my kids to eat outside of the Copamarnia resort. There really isn't any other place to eat without driving. However within 5 miles, in Guanica, there is both a McDonalds and a Burger King as well as a food store. There are restaurants in Guanica but they didn't look inviting to me. There are a number of typical strip mall businesses (K-mart, Walgreens, KFC, Quiznos, high end food store, etc) about 10 miles away in Yauco.If you ask for directions at the front desk there is an area down the coast a bit (20 min) that has lots of restaurants right on the ocean. It is a bit of an adventure if you are up for it. It is not too hard to find but it is further then their map would lead you to believe.The resort is off of a long (3.5 miles) narrow curvy road which makes driving in an out a bit of a hassle but the road looked freshly paved. Speaking of roads, I was amazed at how nice the roads in general are in Puerto Rico. We did eat once at the resort at and had the steak and Lobster ($35 a plate) and it was very good. Outside you can have more casual food like fajitas hamburgers etc for reasonable prices $8 to $15 a plate.Don't pay extra for a Ocean view. All of the rooms have an Ocean view. There are only a couple of rooms (less then 5) that do not have a good view. The view will be better from the 2nd level but having a walkout room is really nice for going to and from the pool. There are 2 pools, 2 hot tubs, 2 kiddie pools, game room. Both pools are large but one is larger and nicer then the other however, that pool is further from the restaurant.The staff is friendly and they speak english. Although I never saw a security guard, I felt very safe there. Someone wrote a review and complained about too many kids and this not being a good place for a honeymoon. I have to disagree. We were there at spring break and the place was dead. There were other families with kids but you often had the hot tub to yourself and 80% of the chairs by the pool were open.There were organized games for the kids during the day but no action at all for kids or adults in the evening. This is not a good place for singles looking to party with others.On our way home we took a different route. We took route 10 up from Ponce across the island. That was interesting but don't do it if you don't have a lot of time. A large part of the trip was on small mountian roads that weren't well marked. However, you are up in the mountains and the scenery is really tropical and pretty.

<Author>YankeeMike
<Content>Beautiful but remote I found Copamarina on the internet, and selected it in part due to previous Tripadvisor reviews. We flew into San Juan, and rented a car. It took about 2 hours to get to Guanica (after a couple minor wrong turns) Unfortunately there were no signs for the resort, and we hadn't thought to get detailed directions. I asked a local cop, and we got a flashing lights escort to the resort! Very nice, even though they spoke no English. Check-in was efficient and friendly. All the staff was very friendly throughout the stay. The grounds were beautiful and constantly being groomed. The rooms were large and comfortable, with a partial view of the Caribbean. There was frequently a nasty low-tide/cesspool smell outside the front door, but it never came into the room. The pools were clean and the perfect temperature, rarely crowded. Some days they had organized pool activities that our kids (12 year-old twins) enjoyed thoroughly. The beach was nice, but there was a lot of seaweed in the shallow water, not great for swimming. We did the all-inclusive, which I would recommend for the meals alone, but it also included use of kayaks and Hobie cat. Lots of good sailing inside the barrier reef with steady breezes. There are 2 restaurants, Las Palmas (outside) and Alexandra (inside) The waitstaff was very friendly, but often it seemed as though they didn't really know how to wait tables. The service at Las Palmas was often intolerably slow. Breakfast buffet was very good. The food at Alexandra was usually very good as well. Guanica is a small town in the middle of nowhere, and there is not much to do outside the resort, We went to the Guanica Dry Forest reserve one day; a unique habitat that was interesting, but that is about it. If you are looking for a comfortable, warm place to enjoy the sun and warm weather, this is it. Overall cost was pretty reasonable, at least for the Caribbean.  
<Date>Mar 30, 2007

<Author>Annes'sspringbreak
<Content>A very special place: My college daughter and I vacationed at the Copamarina in early March 2007. It was a very last minute decision to go and we were so fortunate that we made some great decisions. Traveling without my husband was a first, we felt extremely safe. The resort is so inviting and the staff was engaging and pleasant. The rooms were very comfortable and clean. We loved the cozy outside bar, guitar player and the informal atmosphere. We weren't looking for a disco at night so this atmospere worked well for us. We did all inclusive-for us was probably a good idea. I am a wine drinker but their wine selection was limited. Thankfully, I really did enjoy the wine, not a disappointment. Food was above average, most nights outstanding!The people that work at the resort are very special. Not in your face, but attentive. They really seemed happy to see you each day. Very nice perk!If I had to communicate a down side it would be the beach itself . The seaweed really wasn't a big deal, but you really couldn't take a walk beside the water, even if you left the resort. We decided to get our exercise in the pool . If you want a tranquil vacation, choose the Copamarina. I hope to return with my husband to celebrate our 30th wedding anniversary.Thanks Guys,Pam  Anne, Indiana, PA.

<Author>NestorMitrea
<Content>So Wonderful Our family just got back from a week long stay at the Copamarina. It is a lovely place. The service is incredible, mostly because everyone is just so nice. The staff is friendly but not over friendly. They are always willing to help out - even with requests that are out of the norm. Wilmer who manages the front desk is incredibly sweet and went out of his way to help us when my 8 year old daughter got sick. Raul is an amazing bartender, an artist. My husband will remember his mojitos for a long time. Maria and Robert in the restaurant are great waiters. The rooms are kept clean and they are comfortable. It looked to us like virtually all of them have some view of the ocean. Next time we will choose our room based on location versus ocean view, etc. The walk from the far rooms is more like a hike and with the kids constantly forgetting something in the room, my husband and I felt like ping pong balls. Those rooms are secluded, private and very quiet though. The closer rooms are probably louder but the convenience, for us would be a huge plus. We preferred the rooms on the ground floor as they have access directly to the beach and main grounds but the view from the second floor was better.The food was good and plentiful. We all put on a bit of weight. Alexandra served a paella one night the was out of this world. The only criticism we would offer of the fine restaurant was that it was inconsistent. The food was always good but the same dish didn't taste the same each time. I ordered flan every night and it was different each time. The lobster risotto was to die for two nights in a row. One night it was filled to overflowing with lobster and light on the saffron and the next night it was light on the lobster and had so much saffron that I couldn't' believe it. It was delicious both times just a bit of a surprise.The trip to Gulligan's Island was fun but it wasn't what we expected. The picture in the brochure and dive shop shows a clear white beach... that just wasn't there. We did run into a few other guests wandering around the island looking for the beach. That piece was disappointing. However, It was a great first snorkeling experience for our kids. There wasn't any great coral but lots of fish and it was very manageable and affordable. You can go over there for just an hour which is nice too.Do take the cave hike. It's unique and Irving is a hoot.We did do the all-inclusive and feel that we got more than our money's worth. The bartenders made slushies for the kids all day and we all ate and drank more than our share. The grounds are beautiful and immaculate.One last thing, It was the most mixed crowd we've ever seen on our travels. There were couples of all ages from the very young to the elderly, there were families with young children and families with older teens, there were Americans, Puerto Ricans, Europeans, even a few college kids on their spring break, just everyone. It seems to be a nice, quiet, fun place with a little something for everyone.

<Author>AshNazg
<Content>Beautiful Copamarina I can't say that those who wrote negative reviews didn't genuinely have an awful time here -- but my wife and I definitely had a wonderful stay at the Copamarina. The staff doesn't deserve any of the comments claiming that they were slow and unfriendly. Quite the opposite, I felt that the entire staff was pleasant and everyone we encountered went above and beyond to make sure we were happy. The maintenance staff was especially responsive to a few problems we had, and management offered to upgrade our room even after the trouble had been taken care of. With only a few days of our stay left, we didn't take them up on it -- we were very happy with our original room (Superior Garden View) which was quite large and comfortable.We did not choose the all-inclusive package, which turned out to be the right choice for us. We didn't feel that the food and drinks were sub-par or overpriced, as other reviewers had claimed. We had a great time by the pools, which we almost had to ourselves at times, and also had a lot of fun snorkeling and swimming at 'Gilligan's Island'. It's nicer than the Ca帽a Gorda public beach next to the Copamarina, which we thought was pretty trashy and uninviting. That's hardly the Copamarina's fault, and their own grounds are lovely and well-maintained.The road to the Copamarina isn't 'treacherous' but it is narrow. The edge lines are painted and there is enough room for two vehicles to pass each other, but take your time.In the end, our only real disappointment was that weather changed our plans and cut our stay short by a day. We'd like to close by thanking all the fantastic people who work at the Copamarina for making our visit one of the most relaxing vacations we've ever had.

<Author>SAKANAYA
<Content>Our favorite family vacation spot We stayed at Copamarina for 5 nights after staying 1 night in San Juan (2/20-2/26). We will skip San Juan next time and go to Copamarina straight from the airport as it takes only 2-hour drive. We brought 7 years old and 3 years old, both loved the pool, kiddie pool and play ground. We did not choose All Inclusive package and that was the right choice for us as we saved $1000 over food and activities that we did not do. My husband did scuba diving twice (2 x $90), and I did Bodyderm spa massage ($80), and still saved that much money. We were disappointed that Alexandra restaurant was horrible. I ordered Oriental shrimp and the sauce was totally disgusting - believe me, any Chinese restaurant in your home town can do better. My husband ordered some Italian-like dish with pasta, and we agreed that nothing was fancy. Alexandra was supposed to be fancy with lots of $$$, but food is not worth the money at all. We drove to neighboring town and had much better dinner there. We stayed in Garden View room, but it was a bit small for our family. We looked at the Superior Garden View room and it had more space and looked nicer. Our Garden View room did not have a bath tub (just shower), but we were told that we just needed to ask for it as some rooms have bath tub. The resoft is relaxed and laid back, and stuff were friendly to make us feel comfortable. Overall, we liked this resort and want to go back again.

<Author>mbrebnor
<Content>Nice Resort Copamarina is a nice resort in Guanica, Puerto Rico. Very friendly staff make for an enjoyable stay. The rooms were very nice for the carribean. They are a decent size. We had a nice balcony overlooking the beach and pool area. The food at the restaurants was ok, but the service was great. There is a lot of sea shells.The beach at the resort has a lot of sea grass. If you walk down the beach to the right past the fence, it gets better. Rent a car if you are looking for entertainment because Copamarina is a resort for relaxing. The guitar player was nice at night after dinner.I think the only thing that I didn't like was the picture Id necklaces for the all-inclusive guests. Arm bands would have worked for me. Even though we wore the Id's, the staff still asked for the room number everytime we went to the restaurant or to the bar.We had an overall nice stay at Copamarina.

<Author>attorneyinmichigan
<Content>Overall, the best resort in Puerto Rico First let me see that the food, service and accomodations were WAY above par. Everything was perfect, except for the beach at that specific location. If you like bats, beautiful cactus, limestone caves and lots of interesting birds, the dessert to the north is beyond words - I could go back just for that aspect. Prior to staying here, I did some research on Tripadvisor. Most people were concerned with the beach, which has its problems, but when you compare the best locations in PR, it's at the top of the list. Take El Conquistador for example - this is a great resort with all of the amenities but you have to take a ferry to go to the beach, and there is no snorkeling location nearby. Or, if you were to compare it to Culebra accomidations, you can find a location on Flamenco beach but you have to buy your own groceries. I could go on and on, but the only drawback to this place is the beach, and it is a short ferry ride away to Gilligan's Island, a mangrove outcropping just southeast of the location.So lets talk about the most castigated aspect of this location - the beach. Copa is at the edge of a bay, approximately three quarters of a mile north of the edge of the reef line. As a result, there is little wave action, and LOTS of sea grass. It's just a normal part of that location. It does not feel good on the feet, and I do not recommend going into it - but that's not Copa's fault. Why do I say that? Well, it's very difficult (and for good reason) to get permits to build resorts on or next to reefs because of the damage they tend to inflict in terms of runoff and traffic. So if you want your reef at your doorstep, you may want to go somewhere else where you don't have everything else Copa offers. That said, getting to reef - well, the FISH, in particular, is not difficult. There are four ways to go - a $6.42 ferry to Gilligan's Island, a $45 two hour snorkeling trip, by kayak or by swimming (only skilled triathalets should attempt this). GILLIGANS ISLAND A lot of folks here have critisized Gilligan's Island. Not worth the time, they say - too trashy - no fish, and no reef. Well here is the low down. I went through the island, around the island and on one of the trails. I went everywhere that one could go by foot or by swimming. There are five sections for exploration. The first is by foot. The foot trail on the northern tier is difficult, often slippery, and you WILL find trash nearby. That is because the college kids from Ponce and Mayaguez use Gilligans as a recreational location and are too drunk to clean up after themselves. You will find some of this trash - mostly pop cans - on the northern side of the island, along with sea grass. Although teeming with minows, its a waste of time for snorkelers. Your best bet is outside on the southern, ocean-facing side and the two rivers that stream down from east to west. On the southern, outer edge of the island you will find some of the most beautiful and numerous fish colonies in the Carribean for snorkling (I should know as I've done most). They are under the mangroves and number in the hundreds. If you swim south towards the breaking water (which is about a half mile out) you will find about 20% reef and occasional fish. Be forewarned, however - the current is VERY strong. You should only attempt to swim out to the reef if you have the stamina and endurance to withstand the flow of water. I recommend going along the outside of the northern edge of the island, using the hanging mangroves to steady you against the current, until you get to the far east end of the island.Once you hit the eastern edge you can stand and walk to the river mouth, and then drift snorkle down back to the west end where you first arrived on the boat. There are two rivers that merge into one - the north and south river. I did both several times and the southern one is the best for fish viewing. The trick here is NOT to look down as you won't see anything - the fish are all under the rocks and mangroves, under the shadows. You should wait until noon as there will be less shadow. Here you will find approximately 20 different species of fish, mostly babies, but some very large adults (who are feeding) hiding under the rock. Brace yourself under a mangrove and watch them peer out to see you. Once you get back to near the dock, where most of the people and children are, you might think there are no fish - but alas! There are hundreds. Minows, baby Sergant majors and in the little alcoves, crabs and shrimp. I also saw two VERY LARGE baricuda cruising through for a quick meal.THE SNORKELING TRIPOne thing you should know is that warm weather and hurricanes have done damage to the Carribean reef system, with some reports showing that almost 90% of reefs are dead or dying. This is true, so don't be surprised if you dont see something from the cover of national geographic. That said, there are reef colonies and fish nearby. The snorkeling trip, which is a bit steep, is good to see coral, but not so much for fish. You are basically ferried straight out ot near the breakwater where the reef begins. I saw more fish in one spot at Gilligans than in the entire reef trip. I did see beautiful brain coral, finger coral and other coral colonies on the trip. If you MUST take it, however, you may be able to convince a local in the town nearby to take you there for less. If fish are you thing, stick to the island. It takes some daring, strength and patience, but you will see amazing biodiversity.

<Author>PhiTauBill
<Content>A wonderful, relaxing escape at the Copamarina... My wife and I stayed at the Copamarina from Thursday through Monday in late January and had an excellent time there.We flew into San Juan, and took the hotel's shuttle to and from the airport. Both trips took three hours (traffic slowed us on the way there and a pit stop to pick up an additional passenger that never showed up slowed us on the way back). At $120 each way for two, it was a bit pricey, but we concerned about driving from other reviews we read. The drive is scenic, and not really that treacherous in my opinion. We'll definitely rent a car next time.And I think there will certainly be a next time!The staffmembers were very pleasant (with a few exceptions) and helpful, and the service was quite good (a little slower than we're use to in the states, but we were on vacation, so no worries)We loved the food and the beach. If you get up rather early, you can likely get one of the three four-post beach beds that are very comfortable and I would recommend that you try to spend a few hours of your stay in one.We did the All-Inclusive package, and were not dissappointed (although my pregnant wife would have liked to be able to take full advantage of the free drinks, she like the yummy frozen drinks sans alcohol). The breakfast buffet made for a tasty start to each day. The made-to-order omelets were just OK but everything else was right up our alley. For lunches, we loved the fact that the waiters that worked the beach would bring food in additon to beverages. The Chicken Quesadillas were delicious as was the grilled Tuna. We generally had a snack at the beach in the late morning followed by a late lunch at the outdoor restaurant. We both gained a few pounds from this trip!Dinner was also quite tasty, although we stuck with more traditional dishes like Filet Mignon and Sea Bass versus some of the Puerto Rican Nouvelle Cuisine offerings. We sat in the resturant the first two nights, and reserved outside tables for nights three and four. Our servers were courteous and efficient, and the desserts were tasty, too.As for drinks, the frozen drinks were very good, especially the mudslide. The bartenders worked hard to please, and we tipped them accordingly. I drink mostly beer, and the selection was pretty good for an all-inclusive place (selections included Heineken, Presidente, Medalia Light, and others) and it was always ICE cold.As for the room, we stayed in an Oceanview room, and it was nothing special, but it had everything we needed. We did appreciate having access to the pool and the beach right outside our door!I played volleyball everyday (beware, the ground is particularly hard on the court), and it was a fun game. My wife and I took out the big water tricycle, and it was a workout. The catamarans looked fun, but we did not take advantage. We went ona snorkeling trip that was fun, but we've been spoiled by trips to Maui such that we were a little disappointed in the number and variety of the fish that we saw.The beach was clean, and well maintained, and there just wasn't much to distract us from our reading and sunbathing. It was, in a word, paradise.All in all, I'd highly recommend the Copamarina to anyone who wants a relaxing trip. We did not bring our 20 month old son with us, but know that we will next time, as the Copamarina seemed like a great place for kids. We wanted to check out the villas to see if they would be good for a vacation with my wife's sister, her husband and their kids the next time around, but they were all booked up.We'll report back when we visit again.

<Author>gunner27
<Content>Nice but not my favorite We just returned from staying at the Copamarina. It was nice but we found the front desk staff to have no personality at all. The hotel was clean and the view is beautiful. but after checking in to our room the connecting room wasn't locked and when we opened the door there was another family in the next room - changing no doubt! The safe needed a key that you had to pick up from the front desk (what's the point if the front desk has a key). Dinner at Alexandra was okay but when we asked to sit outside we were told that request couldn't be accomodated. On the whole it's not a bad hotel, it just didn't make us feel welcomed and we usually stay at Ramada's etc. So, we expected to be welcomed when we arrived, paying close to 300.00 a night. There's no vanity in the bathroom only a pedistal sink. The view is beautiful and if you're going to Puerto Rico to read a book then this is the place for you. If you want a friendly atomosphere then I'd go elsewhere.

<Author>mysanibelcondo
<Content>What a great resort! Our family just spent five wonderful days at this resort and all agree it was one of the most beautiful and relaxing places we have stay in the US territories. It is a low-key resort without the hustle and bustle of the large institutions on the East side of the island. Food was very good and everthing needed is right there on the property. It is far from other attractions except the local walks through the Dry Rainforest at Guinica so this is a place to check in and chill out for a few days.Definitely get the all inclusive price that covers all food (three meals daily), drinks, boats, some trips, gratuities plus other perks. The all-inclusive rate is very reasonable for the value it provides.We weren't impressed by the local trip to Gilligans Island but perhaps we missed something.Otherwise, this is definitely a place to go out of your way especially if you are interested in exploring other part of PR outside of the San Juan metro area.

<Author>NMM1027
<Content>Relaxing Vacation My boyfriend and I stayed at the Copamarina in late October and I had to comment on what a fabulous time we had. We rented a car in San Juan and it took us about 2 hours to drive to the resort in some awful weather. The directions were good and the roads were well kept...try to bring some quarters and singles for the tolls. The drive up 333 to the resort starts in a poor area which was sad to see, but it gets beautiful as you get closer to the resort. Stop to take some pictures of the cliffs if you can.The resort itself is very pretty and well maintained and the staff is friendly and helpful. The pools were numerous and all were kept clean and were virtually empty while we were there. The beach was nice as well with clear, calm and warm shallow water. Throughout our stay we felt as if we had the resort to ourselves, even on the weekends when there were many Puerto Rican families there. That was great for us because we went away to relax in peace and quiet and that's exactly what we got. It's a great place to reconnect with your loved one.We had the all inclusive option and highly recommend it since the food is pricey as it is all over the Caribbean. Both restaurants serve some native dishes which were fun to try. The food is not gourmet, but it is mostly good although the dinner options got a little boring by the last night of our stay. The service and food was off one night, but great the other 3.One thing I would recommend against was Gilligan's Island...don't waste your time. It was nothing more then a dirty picnic area with lots of ants. We snorkeled in the mangroves and didn't see too much activity and we caught the very first ferry back.All in all, if you are looking to really get away from it all to relax with your loved one this place can't be beat.  
<Date>Nov 16, 2006

<Content>Very nice overall... Our stay here was very nice overall. Here are some thoughts for your consideration:1.) We are scuba divers and came here specifically to dive. <Content>Copa Marina - - More Than We Expected! My husband and I just returned from our honeymoon at Copa Marina and had to write about our experience! As we walked to the open air lobby to check in we were immediately greeted with warm smiles and friendliness. The staff at the Copa Marina go out of their way to make sure everything is to your liking and are a great resource if you want to go outside of the resort to other points of interest. If you're going to stay at the resort and don't plan on exploring what's outside of it, go all-inclusive. We are planning on going back next year and so are our friends and family. <Author>Annajuliette
<Content>I heart Copamarina Mojiotos! All I can say is amazing! We booked the all inclusive package for 7 days and 6 nights and it was worth every penny. Not only is every meal drink and activity included in your purchase price, even tips are included. (Though our last day there we chose to tip our favorite servers, for making our trip so great.) Because of the time we went (late September) the resort was completely empty. There are pluses and minuses to this. On the good side, service was exceptional, our room was upgraded to an ocean view, and never having to wait for anything was amazing. On the bad side, there was a convention of local priests from all over Puerto Rico that were there that took over the bar every night with the druken anctics. (It was a little odd to see the Padres go wild.) I would highly reccomend this place to anyone that is looking to relax, catch up on reading, good conversation and wonderful mojitos! Do not expect crazy nightlife, though the classical guitar playing out on the patio every night is wonderful! I am planning to go back and hope that others will check it out.

<Author>MLCTC
<Content>Nice resort in quiet location The Copamarina is a solid 3* resort. It offers plenty of space for enjoying a quiet, relaxing time or active amenities such as tennis, swimming, diving, snorkeling and a boat trip to Gilligan Island, a uninhabited picnic and snorkeling island.There is one upscale restaurant Alexandrias which is very good but not exceptional. The other restaurant offers beachside dining and on the weekends an all-inclusive program serving buffet style for breakfast and lunch. They will pack a picnic lunch for you if you are taking a day trip.Service is good, staff is very friendly and helpful. We had a problem opening our in-room safe and the maid took care of it immediately. The room was kept clean and cool. The resort has 2 pools, a hot tub and a wading pool for small children. This is a family resort with limited children's activities.There is a nice game room for the older children and teens andpeddle boats and ski-doos for an extra charge.There is a $15.00 per person beach towel fee which is refunded when you return the towels.The spa was clean and offered typical spa services of massages, facials, and various therapies. There is also a small exercise room with flat screen T.V., weight machine, bikes, eliptical, etc.They have conference rooms and a 3 bedroom private villa.The beach at the resort is kept clean and raked and there are huts, umbrellas and canopied day beds.They also have an on-site dive shop and mini-general store.All rooms have either balconies or patios, cable T.V., 3 phones, in-room safe and unstocked mini-fridge.We were there in late September for 4 days and it was very quiet, with the majority of guests being local Puerto Ricans.I would highly recommend the sunset snorkel trip from La Parquera with the Paradise Scuba and Snorkeling Center to the remote islands, dinner with the owner and an evening snorkel in the Phosphorescent Bay with the dinoflagelites, or a day trip to the Guanica Dry Forest which gets less than 15 inches of rain a year.

<Author>mocha123
<Content>Paradise in Puerto Rico The minute we stepped into the open air lobby, we felt relaxed. We were traveling with a teenage son. We all loved it.The drive from San Juan Airport was not as bad as I thought from other comments. We didn't want to be driving on unfamiliar roads for 3 hours, so we arranged a vacation package with transfers included. Our driver knew the roads well and it took us only 2 hours. The roads were wonderful - large grassy dividers and the most spectacular mountain scenery.The hotel grounds were lush with palm trees, flowers, cacti and succulents. The pictures on the website do not do it justice. My compliments to the landscapers.Our room was not large, but bright and cheerful. Our patio had a ceiling fan with high hedges on each side for a little privacy. Overall, our room was clean, but some attention needs to be given to the baseboards in the bathroom. The bathroom was a nice size with a long counter, but needed brighter lights. These are the only negatives for my entire stay. The shower was wonderful and there was always plenty of hot water. When everything else was so beautiful, I could live with the lighting in the bath. The rooms also had neat shutters which had glass behind them, so you could open the shutters, but not worry about bugs coming in. We did the all inclusive. We were expecting a mediocre restaurant after reading some other reviews, but we loved the food. The breakfasts and lunches were great. Eating these meals outside was pleasant. The made to order omelets were delicious. The chef also made Belgian waffles on request.We looked forward to the dinners. We dressed up a bit and opted for the air-conditioned dining room each night, as we had already been outside all day and we loved the dining room. The staff in the dining room were top notch. They could not have been nicer. Maybe they corrected the problem other reviewers had with dried out food. We ordered our steaks and lamp chops medium rare and they were perfect. The white asparagus with Spanish cheese and ham as an appetizer was delicious. They flavored their little pats of butters with a fruit, I believe it was guava. They were yummy. We had asparagus as a side dish several nights and it was never canned. It was cooked to perfection, with a slight crunch. Don't leave without trying the mango sorbet -- it is to die for! The chocolate sin was also fabulous. We thought this was a fine restaurant. If there was ever a problem, the staff would bend over backwards to remedy it. One waitress even brought out the bag of the type of coffee they used, as I had inquired. I still miss the after dinner Puerto Rican coffees. I enjoyed the house wines, but I don't pretend to be a wine expert. We stayed elsewhere in Puerto Rico after the Copamarina, and I have to say that the Copa's pina coladas were the absolute best. They also made a specialty drink with coconut milk, chocolate and cinnamon that is very good.The beach was great for relaxing. You could pull chaise lounges into the ocean. We wanted to rent a motor boat, but just ran out of time, as we had one day of rain.Gilligan's Island was a lot of fun. We took the ferry. The dive shop employee told us it would take us 20 minutes to kayak there with a group he was taking out. I had seen a woman on the food network (or travel channel) who kayaked to the island and she looked really winded. You are rowing against the current in one direction, so unless you've had some experience, or are in top physical condition, take the ferry. It is further than you think.Gilligan's Island is a mangrove island which has a natural lazy river running through it. I recommend renting fins at the hotel's dive shop to help you swim against the current. You swim all the way to the end, which can take 25 minutes, and then the current carries you back in about 2 minutes. This is the best lazy river you can find. You can also see small colorful fish and tiny crabs on and below the mangrove roots, so take masks. It is not, however, a major snorkeling type area.Security was excellent at the hotel. There were always guards about and they seemed to take their work seriously. The staff was terrific. Everyone was friendly. We had one small glitch where we believe the hotel received incorrect information from the tour company about our transfers. We didn't find out until the night before we were leaving. They had us leaving really early, thinking we had a flight and we did not . We were merely leaving for the Hotel El Convento in Old San Juan and didn't want to leave the Copamarina that early. We did not think they could remedy this situation this late at night, but they did! So we had the entire next morning to enjoy our last breakfast outdoors and take a few more pictures.I want to tell the manager that this is one of the nicest hotels I've stayed at and I hope to return.  
<Date>Aug 10, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice - but be aware Currently in our last day at the resort - we cut it short by a day to stay in San Juan near the airport. Booked it thru Expedia (never again). Copamarina ia a pretty resort with a pleasant staff who were attentive. The service pace is slow - same as everywhere down here.General - The ride in is not a good start - past refineries and a fertilizer plant, down a dangerous 1-1/2 lane road along the coast line, against heavy traffic from the neighboring fenced-in muni-beach. We were pretty wound up before we got to the door. Layout is strange - front desk and bar/restaurant at one end, all of the rooms at the other. Grounds and pools are attractive and well-maintained. Rooms - Just OK - tile floors, but cramped with 2 doubles. Got the Superior room - waste of money-actually furthest from the beach and the desk. Bathroom is a little oversized, but needs some storage for toiletries, etc. Metal doors aren't real attractive, but are freshly painted. TV was out when we arrived - had to call service right away and they responded. Food - One restaurant for b-fast and lunch. Eating outdoors was enjoyable. When that closed at 6, the fancy dinner restaurant opened - but that was all. From 6PM on, no other food (except chips) was available. B-fast was basic, but good. For lunch, had the worst club sandwich ever. Dinner was very good but long. (1-1/2 hrs with no drinks.). No bar with TV - sat in machines in the workout room to see their nice wide screen, but that was locked at 7:00.Services - Wi-Fi internet is available, but we had to sit on the floor near the door to get a good signal. Their hi-speed Internet access itself was down half the time and running on a bad 24K backup telephone line for the whole place. Cell phone service is erratic. Machine wash laundry available - no laundry service. Bell service very liimited. Refrig. in room.Activities - Pools and spas were adequate. Golf 1 hr. away is good enough. Other activities were limited. Scuba, snorkeling and a short excursion to Gilligan's island were available, but some fishing, motorized water sports, diinner cruise or just a boat ride would have been nice. Non-motorized offerings were a little lame. Good tennis courts. BEST FEATURE and high point of trip was hiking in Guanica Dry Forest - just at the end of the road. Our trail went along the rugged coastline and rivals any scenerySummary - I see truths in most of the reviews that I read - good or bad. I can recommend Copamarina - but only as a quiet getaway. Stock up at a local market and hunker down for your stay. But if you like to set up a wide range of things to do - it's just too far from any action (day or nite) to be a good choice.  
<Date>Jun 16, 2006

<Author>shawnh100
<Content>Great Place to Unwind We spent the first week of March at the Copamarina. After dragging 4 kids (10-17) from Vermont to Boston, spending the night in Boston, flying from Boston to San Juan, picking up the rental van, and driving a couple more hours in an unfamiliar place, the Copamarina was quite a sight for sore eyes! Driving into the resort and checking in at the beautiful outdoor lobby, I knew I had made a great choice. We stayed at the Copamarina through our vacation club, so I didn't have to foot the bill for our rooms. Trying to be economical, I had decided not to do the all-inclusive. But after the short, but winding drive to the resort, I changed my mind at the check-in, and bought the all-inclusive for all six of us on the spot. If you have a family, do yourself a favor and splurge on the all-inclusive. It was so nice not to worry about food or drinks...and the kids love getting all those frozen virgin cocktails any time they please. We really enjoyed the daytime staff, especially Ramon (if you see him, ask him for his special drink, it was delicious). If it was busy, they were on over-drive, but when they weren't too busy, they were happy to answer any questions you might have about the area. Many visitors to Puerto Rico never make it out of San Juan, which is really a shame, as the area surrounding the Copa is absolutely beautiful. All the local Puerto Ricans we encountered at the Airport smiled knowingly and told us how beautiful the area would be, and they were right! There are plenty of activities to keep you busy without ever going to town: tennis, kayaking, hiking the Dry Reserve and exploring the cave, visiting other beaches, and going to Gilligan's Island. There was a really nice public beach next to the resort with fabulous facilities, including basketball courts. If you get the all-inclusive, you can check out tennis equipment, the kayaks, beach towels, all sorts of good stuff. Due to the special climate of the Dry Reserve, it rarely rains at the Copa, even when it's raining all over the rest of the island. My family really enjoyed the evening meal together; it was fun to get a little dressed up and take our time enjoying the food. We especially liked sitting out on the patio. The food and service were usually excellent, however, we did notice that when the resort got busier, the quality of both took a little bit of a nose-dive. On the weekends, the resort gets quite busy, as many Puerto Ricans like to come with their families and enjoy the resort. I've found that when locals like to stay at the resort, it means that you're really getting your money's worth, as they are the experts! While you can get all-inclusive at the resort, it doesn't have that impersonal, cookie-cutter feel to it. By the end of the week, it seemed the entire staff knew my family's preferences and routines. While families are certainly welcome there, rude children don't over-run the place; there were couples and singles of all ages that seemed to love it there.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>LOVED it!! Know yourself before you choose to stay here. If you're bored easily by quiet places, or if you require impeccable grounds, four-star dining, and at-your-feet service, go somewhere else! (and don't complain on this site!) The Copamarina is laid-back, but an absolute joy.My boyfriend and I spent four days at the Copamarina, and it was heaven. We are young, but not terribly interested in nightlife -- we're happier to enjoy each other's company in a quiet place. This is the perfect spot for it. We flew in to San Juan from Boston, rented a car and drove to Guanica. The drive was not difficult, but we did run into bad traffic both ways, causing the trip to be around 3 hours -- so be wary of their claim that it's 90 minutes to SJ. It was wonderful to see the PR countryside. After we got there, we only used the car to drive to the entrance of the Guanica Dry Forest.I think the hotel was at or near capacity when we were there, but it never once felt crowded. I was amazed.I grew up in NC and had never been anywhere remotely Carribbean, so when people said the beach was bad I was expecting some kind of dirty black mud. Hardly! It's white sand and clear water. Not much to see in the water, but who cares? Certainly nothing worth complaining about.We had a 2nd-floor gardenview room, which had a nice balcony with a view out over the second (curvier) pool -- nice to sit and read there in the afternoon. It was lovely. I felt no desire to upgrade to an oceanview. We were hardly ever in our room anyway!We did the all-inclusive package based on other reviews on this site, and were happy we did. We enjoyed not having to worry about paying for drinks or finding lunch and dinner. A-i includes all drinks except bottles of wine, for those who are interested -- not to sound like a lush, but hey, these things matter! The restaurant is overpriced and less than stellar. I started to get tired of it after a couple of days. I had one meal that was nearly inedible (rubbery scallops -- a bad choice, in hindsight), but I also had the lamb chops which were really good. The house wine is not so good. I certainly wouldn't be pleased if I were paying full-price for my dinners. Try to get a reservation for a table outside -- it's much more pleasant than sitting inside.My favorite part of the trip was eating breakfast in the open-air cafe every morning. It was sunny and warm and beautiful, and the food was good. It was just the best possible way to start your day. The bacon was perfectly-cooked and plentiful :).The cafe is just a bar at night (no apps available, which would have been nice). It was usually nearly deserted. Sometimes they have live music, which is nice -- but sit far away from it as they turn the speakers up pretty loud so the diners on the restaurant's patio can hear it too.If you have any interest in nature whatsoever, do go to the Guanica Dry forest. There are lots of interesting birds to see early in the morning, and lizards as well. You can get a trail map from the hotel. Be sure to bring water and something to snack on, as it's quite hot when the sun comes up, and the ranger station has no food or drink for sale.Also, if you get the all-inclusive it includes the use of their Hobie Cats, which is a lot of fun. They also have kayaks. We didn't get to go on a snorkeling trip, but I would have liked to.If anyone has questions I would be happy to answer as best I can. I tried emailing the hotel with questions before I went, and I got no response.We will definitely be returning!!

<Author>mayla
<Content>Delightful Place Just returned from a week at Copamarina and can highly recommend it. It is a great family-oriented resort. There is no night life, gambling or shopping. It is located in a very undeveloped section of southwestern Puerto Rico and is peacefully quiet and tranquil. We were told the hotel was full throughout our stay, but it never felt crowded. There are two large pools and two baby pools. The beach is less than ideal because the water is shallow and grassy, but there is a better swimming beach adjacent to the property at a public beach park called Cana Gorda. The restaurant choices are severely limited, but we had a rental car so didn't mind venturing out to explore the nearby towns to find dinner. The room was spacious, pretty and clean. We availed ourselves of the kayaks, hobie cats and paddle boats. We also asked the water sports manager to arrange a jet ski rental one day. That was very fun because there is almost zero boat traffic and very smooth water, making it perfect jet ski conditions. Copamarina is a great destination is you're looking to relax and unwind.

<Author>frunypie
<Content>Loved Copamarina I just returned from Copamarina where I stayed for nine days with my husband and two year old child. To echo previous reviews, the beach at the resort is grassy and yes it's shallow, but it was perfect for my daughter and I didn't have to worry about waves or currents. For those who like to swim, the resort has two pools that were great and very clean. The place was not crowded and is well laid out; even on nights when they were completely booked, it didn't seem crowded. The resort is very low key; the grounds are beautiful. It's true- if you're looking for nightlife, this is not the place for you. It's remote and quiet. The rooms were clean and comfortable; not luxe but spacious and well decorated. I only ate breakfast at the restaurant- which was great- but can't comment on dinners. In general, if you are looking for a five-star dining experience, I don't think this part of the island is for you; you will be better off in San Juan. Overall, it was a great place for a vacation and I would return in a heartbeat.

<Author>cambridgesoa
<Content>Nice place, but service issues.. My husband and I enjoyed our time at Copamarina, but I can say that it is unlikely that we will be returning. The main gripe I have was with the service. Some of the staff was excellent and as courteous as could be (in particular Jonathan who was mentioned in another review and Lizbeth in the dive shop) but others were clearly not making any effort. I have to wonder if this is because many of the patrons of the hotel opt for the all-inclusive option and the staff assumes they have nothing to gain by providing outstanding service? Had it not been for the service issues we encountered, I would likely have given the resort an above average rating. The grounds are well kept, the rooms are decent, the food above average, and there are a number of things to do during the day. Overall it was a nice place to spend a week, but there is definitely room for improvement.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Mid tier resort aspires to improve I had stayed at Copamarina over ten years ago and was apprehensive about visiting again. My fears were allayed, as the resort has improved tremendously. If you are looking for a low-key resort with minimal distractions, Copamarina is a promising choice. The hotel restaurant Alexandra was above average, but in particular we had a waiter named Jonathan who was excellent - very attentive and professional.There are still glimpses of sub-par service (the insolent dinner hostess, the less than perfect cleanliness of the bathroom, the lethargic reception desk staff), but overall my husband and I were pleased with Copamarina. That being said, we do not plan to return.

<Author>BeckyandMike
<Content>Lots of fun!!! We had a great time at the Copamarina! We landed in San Juan and drove to the resort that evening. It is a longer drive fron San Juan than you think it will be because of all the traffic getting out of San Juan, so plan accordingly. Once at the resort, though, we couldn't have been happier. The staff was very accommodating. One morning we had a flat tire, and a young man offered to put the spare on for us, then directed us to a shop just down the road to get it fixed. What could have turned into a big problem somewhere else was just a minor inconvenience for us. We never swam at the Copamarina's beach; it looked a little grassy. But we took the boat to Gilligan's island and had a wonderful time. You have to do this! Definitely bring snorkel gear. The grounds are perfectly maintained, the food and service is great, the rooms are not fancy but are perfectly nice and very clean. We would return! (Incidentally, the second half of our stay we spent at the Villa Montana in Isabela. It was HORRIBLE!!! Don't stay at the Villa Montana--stay at the Copamarina!!!)

<Author>baskin
<Content>Five days at Copamarina We stayed for 5 days at Copamarina in February and I should like to only respond to some issues raised by other reviews. First this is not a luxury hotel with swim up bars but a very comfortable, quiet, and friendly resort. We stayed in a superior ocean front room, which is not nearer the water than some others, but is in a one story building in which there are no connecting doors between rooms. We thus did not hear any activities in the adjacent rooms. The facilities and grounds are very beautiful and clean and we found that everyone was friendly and willing to help. Dinner at the restaurant is excellent with very good service. (Try the fried whole Snapper and one of the Asopaos) The prices are similar to those in Boston. The only exception to peace was one evening when a small business meeting produced throbbing very loud music. Some suggestions relative to excursions that we, and I suspect others, take are the following. LA Montserrate, a restaurant on the south side of Rt. 2 5 miles outside Ponce; excellent seafood on a porch suspended over the ocean: LA Pared Restaurnant in the Posada Porlamar in La Paarguera-excellent inovative and expensive food in a lovely setting; finally try, if possible to get to the Buena Vista Coffee plantation tour on route 123 north of Ponce-English tour at 1:30-need reservations

<Author>Rata
<Content>enjoyed our second stay as much as first My husband and I just returned from our second trip to Copamarina. It's one of the most relaxing places we've ever been to. The grounds are lovely-beautiful palm trees along the ocean. I love the fact the you could see the water from practically everywhere.Never feels crowded.It's very low key and g friendly. Always plenty of places to sit along the beach-either sun or shade. STretch out on a lounge under the covering in the water. The weather was perfect-perfect temperature and very dry, a nice breeze. It looked like a great place to come with young children. My husband was very happy with the dive staff and experience and enjoyed taking the small sail boat out every day-included in the all inclusive. I had a great massage in the spa. We enjoy good food and were very happy with the restuarant-loved sitting outside every evening having a leisurely meal on the patio with the guitarist playing. We always found plenty of selection, especially with the 2 specials every night. The staff in the restaurants were very friendly  worked very hard. Service is slow and relaxing-we enjoy not hurrying thru a meal-we do enough of that iin our everyday life. The all inclusive is definately the way to go. This is absolutely NOT the place to come if you want ritz and glitz, lots of nonstop activity, fancy shopping, poolside service. The last place we went to on one of the other islands was supposed to be one of the top-lots of fancy landscaping, lots going on-very impersonal, had walk to the beach and water-you weren't sure it was there, indifferent buffet dining that made me feel like we were a bunch of cattle. We were very happy to find the Copamarina. Also enjoy exploring the area-liked Ponce, the Tibes Indian Center, and other sites. Though we found that we almost hated to leave the resort.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Place for a Quiet Vacation! My wife and I spent 5 days at this resort earlier this month.Having read the Feb. 17 review by the New Yorkers, I have to wonder if we were at the same resort. For starters, we did not find any of the conditions listed as really bad points or bad points in their review, except that there was no bell hop and no beach side service. BFD!! Our room faced west so we saw a beautiful sunset from our balcony every day. The room had shutters so it was dark-WITH THE SHUTTERS CLOSED- but was light and airy when they were open. The beds (and pillows) were comfortable, and the bathroom was very clean. I belong to two swim clubs and know a clean pool from a dirty pool. I found the pool decks clean and the water gin clear.We ate at the restaurants for five days, and thought the food was excellent, but got a little bored because the printed dinner menu did not change for the five days. We would not recommend this resort for divers as the morning two tank dive left at 7:30am and the afternoon dive only goes down to 20 feet. Also we were told that there wasn't much to see on the reef. So we spent most of our time lounging by the pools, walking the beaches, sailing the Hobies, and ... well, you know.The staff was uniformly friendly and helpful, and fun to get to know.Long story short... we love the Copamarina and would go back again if we wanted a restful, quiet vacation on a secluded part of Puerto Rico.

<Author>Stonescapes
<Content>Wish we could stay much longer!!!!! This is a long review so be prepared. My husband and I stayed one week Feb 4-11 at this lovely spot on the map and came home to a snow storm in New York. I was concerned that we might not be able to go on our scheduled trip due to an unscheduled multiple heart stent proceedure performed on my husband 2 weeks prior. I emailed this concern to the management and before we even arrived Mr.Jose Padin called us to assure us that there was more than adequate health care facilities which he would personally take us to if we had a need. So off we went. To begin with I have many reference points to refer to as I have stayed at many places on the Islands as well as Hawaii. My standards are high and I can assure anyone that this resort is one which is clean and where the people are not intrusive- they care about your comfort, smile, and serve more than most 5 star hotels . We had the mandatory all inclusive plan as we are RCI members. We usually research where we are going to go well in advance. But this pearl of an opportunity came up only one month earlier and we continued to be pleasantly surprised at what we experienced from the moment we were met at the desk by the friendly staff and shown to our room. The room was a little dark due to the shutters, but more than basic in style and all one would need to be comfortable- The bed could have been a little softer but who wants to stay in bed for long anyway while on vacation?? I read the reviews beforehand so we were prepared for a non-typical beach, however typical is not how one would describe the Copamarina! And they make the most with what beach they have. The shoreline is such that sea grass grows, and there is silt from run-off from the beautiful mountains and that is a charachteristic of nature not something the resort can do much about. They keep the grass cleaned up from the sand, have a long dock to walk on or swim from. In addition the cabanas and 4 poster beds on the shore are a lovely touch and oh so nice to lay on after dinner to look at the stars which appear so close or watch a sunset and feel like royalty! There are many water activities at the resort and the $6.00 per. person trip to Gilligans island ended up being magical for us as we snorkled and discovered the newfound strength it took to swim upstream to the ocean and let the current sail us back to the lagoon. One can stay there until 5pm when the last ferry comes. You feel like there are only a few people there even though there are more than a hundred..We went back twice it was so nice and the resort will pack lunch if you ask.. The surrounding beaches on the preserve more than make up for any lacks of a beach at the resort so rent a car to explore this gorgeous picturesque shore line, and do walk the trails. I can still feel the waves at my shins while my feet sink into the sand.. Reuben at the surf shop went out of his way to take us to the cave in the dry forest as it rained on the scheduled day and we were going to leave the next day. He pointed out and remarked about the plant life along the trail on they way there and was so careful of everone's safety as it is a wild cave with no path. He was so friendly and seemed to love his job at the resort. Our stay was all very relaxing and easy to access services as the staff were eager to help.The pools were not crowded and the spa was nice and hot. As pointed out in some reviews, the food at the Alexandra restaurant was not 5 star but was very good, the portions were generous and yes they could expand on the menu for those who stay more than a few days.But it really was all fine for us.Breakfasts and lunches were very good as well with all the variety one could want. The resort grounds were well kept and lovely, and there are many paths to walk. The resort is smack in the middle of a spectacular dry forest and is active in doing their part to concerve,recycle and respect the environment and nature. It is true that even when the resort has many guests one does not feel it. You will find that there are not many people walking around though the place is full! The resort will provide maps if you ask so you can find points of interest to explore.  Commenting on venturing out to see some other parts of the island- We also drove and hiked to the lighthouse at Cabo Rojo and took in breath taking views of the ocean cliffs. While Driving through the towns along the coast one will be struck by the amount of litter the residents leave on the streets of this beautiful island. There are pleanty of garbage bins around, however they don't seem to use them. We also noticed that the local fishermen leave their beer cans as well as assorted nets etc on the shore. We retreaved many clumps of fishing line left on the sea cliffs and even saved a sea turtle from being tangled in it. I am sure if the locals were educated about what effect litter has on the environment and fined if they do it, then maybe it would lessen the amount of bottles, tops etc. left around. I know this goes on in all states, but it is really noticable among such beauty of Puerto Rico as it is such a contrast. It is a sad reminder that our planet is being smothered by plastics and the many conveniences of our modern society. Also there are many roaming dogs on the island. I wish some vets would volunteer their time and spay a few dozen once a month in all the towns until the problem is under control.I don't think we will see any TV shows on Animal control in Puerto Rico anytime soon. It was hard to see the bones of the skinny ones and the tired looking nursing females that roamed in small packs. Perhaps that is why there is not alot of visible wildlife, as the dogs kill and eat what they can find in the forest and on the island. There were also quite a few thin horses left to graze where they can in some towns. Those things were the only sad part of our trip which had nothing to do with the resort.  On a brighter note we also visited the art museaum in Ponce and viewed their magnificent collection of art, but there was not enough time to see much else and there is much to see in Ponce! We also wanted to visit the caves at Camuy Park, and the National forest but could'nt. So much to see so little time, so we will just have to come back! The magestic mountains and valleys on the 100 mile trip back to the airport was truely a visual treat and put more icing on the cake! As for us we would love to return to the Copa Marina it was a trip we will always remember with a smile, no- with many smiles as it is a unique, special place. I wish we were still there and yes we would love to return.

<Content>The Good, the Bad, and the Ugly! My husband and I are still here and this is our last day of four. I will start by saying I would have rated it 31/2 if that was an option. Here it goes:The Good: People could not be nicer, more helpful or harder working. So management...compliments to your staff. Good size rooms, clean with pleasant view and good housekeeping. Dinner in the Alexandra Restaurant is relaxing with nice back round music from a live guitarist. The pools are refreshing, clean and never crowded. The beach is certainly not one of the best but again you can swim out or use their water sports if you choose. The BEST Margaritas! Very quiet and comfortable no one intrudes on your space. You can be very casual no matter where you go on the property.The Bad: Very tired and in need of updating. The rooms are good size but very dark because of the shutters no light gets in. The shower takes for ever to drain, bathroom is small,the amenities are average(that is all related to price). Grounds could be exceptional if they added some color and maintained it better. If you are only going to have one restaurant open for dinner, change the menu. Food is average. Staff not trained right....no reason to wait for drinks from your server while three other's are standing around. The Ugly: There is none. If you are looking for a happening spot with exciting night life, great restaurants and non stop activities...this is not the place for you. Go to San Juan.TIP: The All-Inclusive option is very good. It includes taxes, resort fees, etc.

<Author>marketom
<Content>Nice but not perfect Copamarina was a nice resort but not perfect. What we liked: It is located in a secluded dry tropical forest area on a beautiful area of the coast. The grounds were pretty and child-friendly with a wading pool and a playground. It is a nice low-key resort (which is what we were looking for). And we really enjoyed our visits to the village of Guanica, which in our experience was full of friendly people.What could have been better: most of the staff was unusually unfriendly. When we arrived, we were greeted by a very crabby girl at the front desk who looked very annoyed that we had arrived. For our three days there, we did not have one friendly experience at the front desk, even when just asking a simple question. Most of the bartenders were equally unpleasant. During our stay, the only friendly staff was one waitress and housekeeping. The highly acclaimed restaurant, while good, seemed less professional than we would expect for the prices. For one of the finest restaurants in Puerto Rico, we were surprised to find what appeared to be canned asparagus (certainly not fresh) in our food. We had a waitress who was nice but was unable to give us a single recommendation from the wine list to pair with our meal. The restaurant was pretty good, but in light of the prices and acclaim we thought it would be a more refined experience.But overall I have to say that we had a nice time at Copamarina and enjoyed our stay at the resort and in the area -- and it certainly was a nice break from the bustle and noise of San Juan.Tom S.Chicago, IL

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect Getaway - but have a car My husband and I stayed at the Copamarina Beach Resort from December 19th through the 24th. If you like city life, having multiple choices of restaurants and other recreational activities at your disposal, this is not the place for you. We went right before Christmas and it was fairly quiet. We paid about $170 per night, which was on the border of our budget, but worth the money. The weather was fantastic - in the 80s each day and sunny. While the resort has all of the amenities, unless you like to sit and lounge around all day doing absolutely nothing, you will be bored. We recommend going kayaking out to Gilligan's Island. If you rent the kayak from the resort, it will cost you $20/hour. If you go to the Gilligan's Island ferry dock, which is literally within a 10 minute walking distance, it will cost you $10/hour. The Caribbean is calm, shallow and warm here so kayaking is a pleasure. The room we had was very clean and on the first level with a garden view. We much preferred this room to one with a beach view, not only because it was priced a little less, but because there was much less traffic outside of the room. I agree with the other reviewers' assessments of the sound problem. You can hear everything and it's mainly because of the connecting door between rooms. The management should strongly consider replacing these doors with those that are more soundproof. The bathroom could have been cleaner, but I am a stickler about bathrooms - I check under toilet rims and look carefully at shower drains and shower heads. Management should pay more attention here.We thought the restaurant served wonderful food - particularly the fried red snapper. It is pricey and not something I would recommend doing every day. Don't get the package deal unless you plan to spend the entire day at the resort and drink lots of alcohol. It is a waste of money.The gym was perfectly fine for our needs. Unfortunately, I did not try the spa. Perhaps next time.Go to the Bosque Estatal de Guanica. It is truly for nature lovers and the climate and biome probably one of the most unique in the world. Drive into Ponce and spend an afternoon at the Ponce Art Museum, then eat at El Bohio, if you can find it.My husband and I came here without our children, but it is a great place for kids too. We saw many during our stay. Copamarina is a great resort if you want some peace and quiet, but bring a car. It is fun to explore and drive on the winding, hilly roads. We drove all over the southern and western parts of Puerto Rico during our stay and feel that we got a much better sense of the island and its culture.

<Author>dbosullivan
<Content>Don't know where these other reviewers stayed My girlfriend and I just returned from Copamarina- what a letdown. On previous trips to PR we stayed at the Rincon Beach Resort in Anasco, but we thought that we should try something different. So much for variety being the spice of life. The hotel is isolated, with absolutely nothing nearby. We were given a room literally a quarter mile from the front desk (and the only open bar). They had serious issues with their leach field/septic tank, and the odor was very offensive 24/7. The housekeeping service was the only staff that we were happy to deal with. Otherwise, poor service was the norm. If you stay here, expect nothing nearby in terms of amenities, deposits for beach towels, and a disappointing shoreline. If you're planning to go somewhere in Puerto Rico, make it Vieques or Rincon- don't bother with this place.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Trapped This is the first time I strongly disagree with other's review on trip advisor about a hotel. We found the Copamarina was not worth the money we paid. (about $850 for 3 nights) In spite of this and the fact that our room was prepaid we left the hotel a day early. I felt trapped on this property and was so relieved when we finally decided to leave in spite of losing money on the room we had paid for.  Yes the property was pretty but there was only one restaurant that served lunch and one that served dinner. The prices were very high. So if you have already decided to go to this property I would take the meal plan. One Restaurant was opened at a time, that is your only food option... unless you have a rental car and wanted to drive up the mountain on a winding road about 15 minutes to the Guanica waterfront where you'll find a place to eat and a couple of local bars. The road is narrow and the curves are sharp. The hotel has one bar, the same outside location where lunch and dinner is served.  There's no room service. The dive shop that hands out the beach towels opens at 9am. (yet the young lady in the dive shop was extremely nice!!) Our television had horrible reception. Our room was not ready when we arrived at 3:45pm.  The property and the rooms were clean. The Beach was nice. Personally I did not think the hotel was worth the price. It is so isolated I could have been on a beach in Florida. It depends on what you are looking for, but I wish I had this advice before I made my reservations.
