<Content>Just terrific ! My 5 night stay must have coincided with the traveller from Boston; their very comprehensive review says it all! I would agree completely and would add....The service in the Alexandra restaurant warrants huge praise. Someone has Ritz-Carlton training and has brought it to Guanica. <Author>luvzsun
<Content>The Perfect Do-Nothing Vacation My wife and I like 鈥渄o nothing鈥?vacations 鈥?we don鈥檛 want adventure or excitement, just a beach, some shade, plenty of tropical drinks, nearby bathrooms, and time to plow through a stack of paperback novels. Above all, we don鈥檛 want to think or make lots of decisions on vacation (we get enough of that at work).In January 2006 we had a wonderful 8-night stay at Copamarina, and plan to go back next year. We had the all-inclusive package, and felt it was a great value. We did rent a car in San Juan and drove down to Guanica, through once we got there we never left the resort. The drive from San Juan was pretty straightforward and about 2.5 hours in duration (with traffic). There are several toll roads so bring a roll of quarters (the exact change lines are far shorter than the cashier lines). The roads are standard U.S interstate type roads, and the only narrow, twisty part is the last 5 miles from Guanica to the resort (but still well-paved). Our Garden View room was very nice 鈥?the usual amenities and air conditioning. All the room balconies/patios face the ocean, so the difference is really how many palm trees and pools you want between you and the Caribbean. We didn鈥檛 feel like the Ocean View option was a major plus over the Garden View rooms (given how close the beach is). The palm trees and flowers and the entire grounds are well-maintained and beautiful.We were also very pleased with the friendliness of the staff, from the wait staff in restaurants and bar to the water sports staff and the grounds crew. Almost everyone speaks English. All our requests were met promptly and with a smile.Copamarina serves a breakfast buffet from 8-11am, which never varied but was pretty good for resort faire. They had an omelet station, plus scrambled eggs, bacon, sausage, fried potatoes, fruit, pancakes, and French toast. We never got tired of it in eight days.Lunch is from 11am-6pm, and the menu is a mix of sandwiches, burgers, salads, and dinner-type entrees like steak, fish, and chicken, all served in their outdoor bar/caf茅. Overall, we were quite happy with the variety and quality of the food and the service 鈥?just enough variety for about a week. Many people got their food 鈥渢o go鈥?to either eat on the beach or their room or take it with them on a trip somewhere.Dinner was from 6-10:30pm or so, and was a white-table-cloth affair, though not necessarily that formal 鈥?people were in everything from dresses to t-shirts and shorts. They had a nice selection of appetizers and about 12 entr茅e items, plus a daily fish or meat special. We tried just about everything on the menu, and the variety was also just about right for a week鈥檚 stay. You had the choice of eating inside or outside, and outside they had an acoustic guitar player providing music nightly.We spent most of our time sitting in beach chairs reading books, and overall were very happy with the general layout. Southern-facing beaches often have little shade, but the Copamarina had enough palm trees, umbrellas, and thatched canopies so that we had no trouble staying out of the sun. They probably have about 40 beach chairs, and we only saw about 1/3 of them in use at any time. As others have written, the only downside to the beach is the water. The beach itself is quite nice (good clean, white sand) but from the edge of the water to about 100 feet offshore the water is only about 1 foot deep and there is quite a bit of silt on the bottom. If you walk more than about 20 feet into the water your feet sink several inches into the silt, so the immediate shoreline is too shallow and mucky for much recreation. However, the resort has a 100 foot dock, and off the dock the water is deep enough for swimming. The resort is in a protected cove, and in January (with prevailing winds from the east) there are only about 1 foot waves at most, so no chance for boogie boarding or playing in the waves. There were a few scattered patches of grass in the shallow water, but since we didn鈥檛 spend any time there (and they weren鈥檛 visible from the beach) the grass didn鈥檛 detract from the view. The shallow water and silt was definitely a detraction, but the rest of the resort made up for it.As far as watersports, Copamarina has two Hobie Cats, a bunch of kayaks, and some pedal-type watercraft. Given we had the all-inclusive package, we went out several times in the Hobie Cat and kayaks. No complaints there 鈥?all the equipment was in great shape and the water staff were quite helpful. They also offer dive instruction and dive tours, but we didn鈥檛 do any of that.The resort has two swimming pool areas, each with a separate hot tub and kiddie pool. Instead of cooling off in the ocean, we took a dip in the pool or hot tub every few hours. The hot tub was quite nice in the early evening. You can鈥檛 beat the proximity from hotel room to beach (and thus a nearby bathroom and air conditioning) plus clean beach towels every day.We loved the all inclusive package, and felt it was a great value. We lost count of how many drinks we ordered from the bar and brought to the beach (during the afternoons the staff would make an occasional trip down the beach to take orders too), and we liked not having to look at prices and calculate tips. Since we didn鈥檛 have to wait for a bill or sign anything, meals and drinks were also more efficient. Our usual vacation strategy has been to eat one or two meals a day in restaurants, and then buy our own breakfast/sandwich stuff and drinks at a local grocery store and eat the rest of our meals on the beach or in our room. Based on our calculations the all inclusive package was pretty much equal to what we鈥檝e paid in the past for hotel, meals, and drinks on other trips, and this time we didn鈥檛 have to hunt for provisions or throw away excess stuff when we returned home. Overall, the all inclusive package just made our lives easier.Again, we never left the resort once in eight days. The southwest part of the island is pretty sparse compared to the northern side, but we heard there were interesting museums and shopping areas in nearby Ponce. Other vacationers reported they did some hiking in the rain forest. There is also a ferry that runs from the Copamarina dock to a nearby island with a better beach and snorkeling opportunities (we didn鈥檛 do that either).Overall, we loved our stay at Copamarina. Though we wish the water at the beach was deeper and the ocean floor was less mucky, the rest of the resort鈥檚 amenities, layout, service, and overall value more than made up for it. For those out there like us who just want to read books and vegetate for a week, Copamarina is a great place.

<Content>Friend....its the Best kept secret in Puerto Rico! If you have a family or its you and the love of your life. Go here! I probably don't have enough room to write how much I enjoyed the hotel, the staff, the food, the guitar player, the gift shop, the service, the breakfast, the dinner, the restaurants, the drive, the pools, the location, etc.etc.etc.... but I'll try to squeeze it in.My wife (pregnant at the time), myself, my 2 year old and my 9 year old arrived in San Juan in the morning and took the 3 hour drive through the heart of Puerto Rico through Ponce and on into Guanica. Precise!Now you know those winding roads that are on the side of mountains in the movies....well once you leave the highway and turn onto the main road leading to the resort that's exactly what you're going to be on....so slow down...and no drinking and driving...because the car coming around the corner head-on is driving in the same lane as you are.That's 98% of the bad stuff I have to report.Beautiful! Gorgeous! Just overwhelmingly nice and pleasant. Our luggage was late by a day...airline's fault. But the staff not only showed empathy but kept me posted with hourly updates on their communication with the airline and the courier.We had an excellent room. Excellent house keepers. Excellent cooks...especially Louis during breakfast hours.The only warning I have...and the resort warns you as well......Do Not Feed The Birds! These creatures are the only birds I have ever seen with pupils and they will swarm you if you offer one of their kindred a morsel...its like they hang out in the trees above and wait for some poor sucker to let down his/her guard....then POW!...they're on you and its too late. They remember to. They will be back...for breakfast, lunch, and dinner...at your door...no one else's....Your Door.Because of the mountain range the area gets very little rain...it literally rained 30 seconds while we were there...and it was more like the sky spitting on you if you can call that rain.This is relaxation at its finest...if you are a city guy or gal and are looking for night life....you're 3 hours away from that. Sorry. But if you want QUIET...Beauty...fresh air...Copamarina is the place.We're going back....and we're bringing others.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>It was just about perfect The hotel and grounds are beautiful. Several very nice swimming pools. We checked out the other reviews and they are on the mark. It IS remote so the all-inclusive plan is by far the best way to go. Alexander's Restaurant has excellent (excellent!) food for dinner. The service was pretty good. La Palma restaurant for breakfast (very ample and varied buffet) and lunch is open air and very nice. The service staff is particularly warm and attentive. The beach is as others have said - somewhat muddy, somewhat with sea grass - but little wave action so it's good for children. 300 yards walk down the beach to the west is a very nice public beach with no grass (but still a little cloudy). We found beaches about 2 or 3 miles drive past the hotel (on 333) to the east. These beaches have more wave action and are clear of turbidity and grass. The road to the resort is nicely paved, with ample guardrails, and very curvy. Just go slow and stay on your side and there's no problem. All-inclusive includes kayaks (one and two man), 2 catarmerans, pedal boats and were readily available.We had a miscommunication with the hotel that could have turned out to be unpleasant but the hotel corrected everything and was most accomodating. Clearly the hotel is well run. Things go very smoothly.Gilligans Island trip was hardly worth it. Just a small shallow, sandy lagoon surrouded by mangroves. The locals seem to gather here. We left on the first boat back.Note: Beware of radar traps throughout Puerto Rico. We got a speeding ticket (65 in a 55 zone) just as the limit went from 65 to 55. Saw many, many police cars and drivers getting tickets during our 5 day stay. It seems to be an income stream for the island. If you rent a car (which most will do), strictly obey the limit.

<Author>MercerChow
<Content>Fine place to get away - really away Our family of six spent a week at the Copamarina and had a fine time. I will not repeat what others have said about the facility itself, swimming, etc.; there were no surprises. If you like hiking or birdwatching the adjacent dry forest is terrific, many trails and easily accessible. The Copamarina is also a good base for exploring the entire SW coast of PR, from Ponce around to Mayaguez - each about an hour east or west, respectively. There are several other good PR and US natural reserves within that span, especially Cabo Rojo, Boqueron, and Laguna Cartagena.Because we took many day trips we did not stay on the all-inclusive and therefore the Alexandra restaurant was too pricey for a la carte every night. There are few dining options in Guanica proper but several good ones in Parguera, about 20-25 minutes west. The informal Las Palmas was a better value for breakfast and lunch.As far as day trips go, one word of warning. The Arecibo Observatory and Rio Camuy Caverns are not as accessible from Guanica as they might appear on a map. There are no good roads across the Cordillera, and Route 10 does not go straight through, despite what it says on several maps. Be prepared to spend some considerable time on narrow, winding mountain roads. (They make the 333 road into the Copamarina a piece of cake by comparison.)If you do go to Parguera do not bother with the trip to the Bahia Fosforescente. The lights are gradually going out and I feel sorry for the boat operators who are still trying to squeeze a living from this dwindling resource. But it's underwhelming, believe me.For a bit of culture, the art museum in Ponce is an absolute gem - a world-class collection in a beautiful but modest and manageable space (designed by the same architect who did the MOMA in NYC).Would we go back to the Copamarina? Tomorrow, if we could!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolute Paradise We went on the recommendation of the majority of reviews on this website, and we were not disappointed. This place is fabulous to just go and get away from it all. The all-inclusive is the only way to go IF you are planing on staying on the grounds your entire trip. Food is excellent and well worth it. Drinks are top shelf, and Raul is the finest bartender we have ever had the pleasure of meeting. It does get a little busy on the weekends because a lot of the locals from San Juan go here on getaways, but once Sunday afternoon rolls around you have the place to yourself. There were families at the resort, but to me it seems to be more for couples looking for a romantic getaway. The beach is not really for swimming, but there is a very nice beach within walking distance right next door. Driving to and from is a little crazy, but just take your time and everything is fine. Staff was excellent, we will be going back!

<Author>lauramh
<Content>Nice resort but far away I stayed here in June 2005 to go scuba diving. I had done a lot of research and was glad I purchased the all-inclusive option. Otherwise, there's very few restaurants in the area and the on-site restaurants can be expensive if you pay as you go. My only complaint about the room was that the A/C unit is one of those large noisy units that sits in the corner. I had a hard time falling asleep with it running. But the weather was too hot to turn it off. The food was excellent, sometimes the service was slow but it wasn't a problem. The on-site dive operator was great, they have a very nice boat and the divemaster was really professional. The dive sites are nice and the reefs are healthy. Believe what others tell you about the Copamarina beach. Pretty muddy and some sea grass. The road to get to the Copamarina (route 333) is very treacherous to drive. Very narrow and you hope that cars coming the opposite direction are paying attention. The resort is on the southwest corner of the island, a good 2-3 hours from San Juan by car. This is a resort that is best enjoyed if you either come and stay without leaving, or keep your daytrips to points close by. A trip to El Yunque, for example, is approximately 3 hours by car each way.

<Author>carlo45
<Content>Beautiful Resort and great food and facilities We chose Copamarina based on the reviews here and we wanted the carribean side of Puerto Rico since the weather is more reliable. It's a 2 hour scenic drive from San Juan but worth the drive to be in one of the more beautiful areas of the island. The place is absolutely beautiful and not one complaint from my wife and two teenagers. One of our best family vacations. Find a nice lounge chair and let all your tension roll away. The resort offers something for everyone. I think the all-inclusive is the biggest bargain of all vacations considering the quality of the food. When my teenagers heard all-inclusive they immediately thought buffet and cafeteria style. Instead it was two restaurants with excellent menus and food. Dinner is served in a beautiful restaurant called Alexandra with superb quality and service. All drinks, day and night are included too! We have stayed in more expensive places in Puerto Rico and paid double the price for half the beauty and amenities. There is lots of boating and water activities. If you want a big ocean with waves this is not the place for you although other guests took day trips to nearby beaches where they could boogie board. Copamarina is on the gentle carribean sea, my preference. I especially enjoyed kayaking and sailing the hobie cat which is also included in the all inclusive.The grand surprise is the snorkeling. For beginners or experienced, it's only an 8 minute boat ride from the hotel dock and you will dive into a tropical paradise.

<Content>Best for couples. We had a wonderful stay at the Copamarina. I would rate is as 8 out of 10. The positives are as follows: a. The location is private.b. <Author>momwith3kids
<Content>Nice resort, but no five star We stayed at the Copamarina Resort in October to celebrate my in-laws 40th anniversary. My husband, 3 kids, (ages 7,5,3), mother in law, father in law and brother in law all spent four days there in the pouring rain. The resort is very pretty, very secluded and quiet and has a wonderful staff and restaurant. The things to be aware of, however, are these:-- the beach is not nice. Seaweed, and debris from all of the trees were all over the sand. The bottom was more like a lake than the ocean. My kids wouldn't have put a toe in, and they love the beach. It's true, there is a public beach a quick walk away, but not what you expect from the Caribbean. -- the Villa, which is two 3 bedroom apartments, one on top of the other has no air conditioning in the common rooms. Because of the size of our party, we had reserved this and we moved immediately. While nicely decorated and spacious, we couldn't suffer the heat anytime we weren't in the bedrooms.-- they advertise 4 pools. Two are tiny kids pools, and not the sort that keep any kids over the age of 1 occupied. That left two pools to enjoy. Just a note if you're planning a long vacation and want a variety of pools, with interactive things for the kids, you won't find it here.-- On the positive, the restaurant is excellent. We ate every meal there, and were not disappointed. The road leading to the resort is very winding and narrow. Because of the terrible weather, we never left for me

<Author>mella1
<Content>Copamarina was great! We just returned from the Copamarina and it was fantastic. Even though it was rainly season and the weather was not too cooperative, we still had a great time. The resort is very lovely- clean and beautifully lanscaped. We were upgraded to a superior garden room however, we still had full view of the ocean. The room was also a great size and very cozy and clean. They have cable TV which, given the weather was a blessing.I cannot say enough about the staff. They are unfailingly nice and very helpful. From the front desk staff to the waiters, there was no one that wasn't extremely cheerful and helpful.I would recommend the all inclusive option. We did not find places to eat in the immediate area and the menu at the Copamarina was quite expensive. Here all inclusive means eating resturant style with snacks and drinks available any time.The only disappointment was Gilligan's Island. We found it to be a very small beach and the snorkling (equipment included in all inclusive) was very so-so. The water is beautiful however- crystal clear and just what you's expect from the Caribbean sea.Copa is definately worth a visit.

<Content>Copamarina: very friendly place We stayed at the Copamarina from 08/08-08/14 with 2 small children, ages 5 and 2 and everyone had a blast.Food: it was delicious, I gained 5lbs in a week, rice and beans w/pork chops everyday and flan everyday. All the pools are very nice.Activities: There was always something to do, thanks to Irving in the dive shop. He organized kayaking race for the kids, vollyball, treasure hunt, to name a few. He was very helpfull. Copamarina is definitely a place for families, couples, singles, seniors, everyone.Management: The management was very gracious. My 5ys old son sone stepped on a rusty nail in the outside resturant and the management and staff was very responsive and apologetic. They escorted my husband and son to the hospital, paid for his medicines, and even gave us an extra day for the rental car so we could do more sightseeing. Thank you all very much, especially to Mr. Jose Padin, the General Manager. Also, I left my credit card in the dive shop and they returned it to me while I was having the yummmy dinner. Your honesty is appreciated. BTW, the rusty nail was removed from the restaurant.The island of Puerto Rico is very beautifull. The rainforests are magnificent, the bamboo trees are so gracefull. The people are nice. Copamarina is a wonderfull place to stay while enjoying the beautifull island of Puerto Rico.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lovely time, lush dinners An extraordinary time to relax, catch alot of sun, and enjoy wonderful service from all the staff. A group of 10 adults recently visited this terrific, all inclusive resort and found a very relaxing atmosphere away from the hustle and bustle of a big city like Chicago. The 2.5 hour ride from San Juan to Guanica was picturesque and quite lovely. The drivers spoke plenty of English, knew their way around to make a snack run, and even took you to a bakery for some deep, rich cafe con leche. Don''t worry about the way everyone else drives in PR( fast/furious), these drivers know their business. The magic of the hotel restaurant, Alexandra, is in their cuisine- first class and easy going. Breakfast is a big buffet so enjoy!! Lunch and dinner are meant to be completed in several hours so remember this as you order your food. The service folks are outstanding so remember them as you tip! The grounds are lush, with plenty of chairs to sit at by the pools, on the beach( go to the public beach- if you want to swim in the ocean, or on Gilligans Island) and bring ALL your own supplies to use. The front desk staff are ALL friendly, helpful, and accomodating. Don't be shy- ask the staff for help in renting a car or van, be sure to plan with 24 hrs notice.( A car is really important if the family gets itchy to do something) Ponce is 45 minutes away with a great Art Museum, lovely historical museum and a great area to do some bargain shopping near Fireman's Park(Parque de los Bomberos) People are friendly so ask if someone speaks English- Try your Spanish, it's appreciated. If you visit the Cave, be sure to wear sneakers, long pants, baseball cap, and gloves you will throw away. Any child over 12 would be fine to go into the Cave. Any child over 8 for the walk in the Dry Forest. Anyone under 8, visit the beautiful beach that is close by! The kyaking, diving, sailing and other activities are all arranged in the Dive Shop- the young, cute, beautiful and handsome staff will take care of the arrangements. Ask the Captain of the Diving boat about the illegal member of his family- Great storyteller! Overall, enjoy the pace of life in Guanica- slow and steady- Enjoy the drinks, delicious and lastly, enjoy la isla del encanto.

<Author>giolo
<Content>Was Amazing... How can you go wrong for an all inclusive for two people, $328.00 per day. All you can eat, all you can drink with gratuities included. I can not say it is a five star hotel, but it was clean, the room was large and very comfortable. The staff was great. I asked if there was anyway I could get a surprise cake for my husband for our anniversary and the girl at the front desk went out of her way and bought one for us. The food for us at least was not the best we have ever had, but we have had worst. Location can not be beat. The hotel was quiet and relaxing. There were two days when we had the pool all to ourselves, I mean how can you complain. We took a day trip to Bahena Beach (spelling probably wrong sorry) and the water was incredible. People did leave behing their garbage which is a disgrace but if you can see beyond that it was amazing. You can actually walk in the shallow water and see not only your feet but tons of fishes. The Copamarina was a relaxing vacation and that is what we wanted. Like others have said if you are looking for five star quality food, a nightlife this is not the place for you, but if you are looking for a hideaway with great staff and amazing views of palm trees and the bluest water this is the place. Any questions Please feel free to ask

<Author>Piolina
<Content>Paradise! We stayed two nights last weekend at the Copamarina and it was a bliss. Although our room was supossedly garden view we were upgraded to an ocean view room. It was very neat, not pretentious, but with all the basic needs. Tropical decoration, soap and shampoo dispensers in the shower, wireless internet and cool drinking cups that make a nice souvenir. I also loved the futons on the beach! The staff was very friendly and the secluded location was great for those wanting to relax and feel away from everything. It is also close enough to take a day trip to Ponce and a visit to La Parguera and the bioluminiscent bay. The hotel beach was not good but next to it was Ca帽a Gorda, a public beach great for swimming. Their kiosko had excellent local food (empanadillas) and cheap pi帽a coladas, wich made a nice lunch. The only cons of the hotel are the beach and the pricey restaurant. Although food was pretty good, it was expensive. And the only option for breakfast is a buffet, so if all you want is some coffee and bagels/pastries it is definitely not worth the price.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Place For Scuba Just got back from a very relaxing Memorial Day weekend trip to the Copamarina resort. We did two two-tank dives on Saturday and Sunday that were filled with beautiful coral and lots of marine life. The crew was very professional, safe, and fun. Costs: $165/night (minus a 10% discount for AAA) for a very clean and comfortable room that overlooked the caribbean ocean and included a daily buffet breakfast. The bathroom was rather large w/ a hair dryer and seemed like it was recently remodeled. Diving cost $95 for the first day of diving and $85 for the second day (all equipment included--make sure you have your dive card). You may be able to talk them down on this price if you have a large group. Beware, the time on the boat can get very wavy...so if you get sea sick, take the appropriate meds.The food was great. Breakfast was $16.00/person for an all you can eat buffet, Lunch menu was similar to a Ruby Tuesday/TGIFriday's type menu and prices were also comparable. Dinner was excellent at the only restuarant that is open after 6pm. The resturant is very classy with inside and outside dinning with prices ranging from $22-30 per meal. The apple dessert $7.00 wasn't that great. Overall, a great stay at a pretty good price. I would recommend this hotel and dive shop to anyone who is interested in diving Puerto Rico.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic Getaway My husband and I spent four nights at the Copamarina from May 9-13th. We loved our time here! We were in San Juan for four days prior and it was a great contrast. San Juan is busy and you are always running around, The Copa is quite and peaceful. The resort is beautiful with so lush gardens, a great ocean view and it is nestled in a scenic and nature filled area. If you are looking for some rest and relaxation or some advenuture this is the place for you. We found the English speaking staff so friendly and helpful. More than one time, they told us don't worry we will take care of it, you are on vacation. It was music to our ears. We enjoyed their pools, beach, and activities such as the cave hike and kayak tour of Gilligan's Island. Just note, the other reviews are right, the beach on the property is not for swimming. You can walk less than 50yards to the public beach or drive 5 min past the resort to another beach. The gym was good and the massage at the Bioderm Spa a real treat. We opted for the all inclusive which worked out well. You have more than enough choices and options. The food is great. Dinner is in a nice restaurant with live music and excellent cuisine and service. We found that t his is a great place to relax and take it easy. Enjoy your stay! We look forward to our next trip to the Copamarina.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful place to unwind, hike, snorkel My wife and I went to Copamarina in April 2005 and had a wonderful time. The grounds are lush, the food was terrific, the rooms and the staff were very nice. A few tips:-- If you want to snorkel out on the reef, reserve as soon as you can. Spots on the boat filled up quickly the week we were there.-- Copamarina's beach is nice for relaxing in the sun and taking dips in the pools and saunas. If you wish to swim in the ocean, it's shallow and grassy. But not to worry. The lovely Cano Gorda public beach is right next door, a stroll of maybe 200 yards. It has a sandy bottom and lifeguards.-- The sandwich shop at Cano Gorda is great for a quick lunch. The sandwiches are just $2 or $3. The pina coladas are cheap.-- If you go to Gilligan's Island, there is a coral reef just off the island's western tip. As you walk off the dock, take a right (most people will be turning left), duck through the fence, and pick out a picnic-table shelter as close to the western edge as you can get.-- Gilligan's Island gets its nickname from the lagoon, which is actually a tidal stream moving through the mangroves. Going up river against the current is a bit of work, but your reward is a chance to snorkel as you float back down to the lagoon. Very relaxing. Lots of fun.-- The rooms were nice with fridge, safe and balconies or terraces. The TVs had English-language cable (CNN, ESPN, HBO, etc.) as well New York City local channels.-- The ocean is very clean because the resort is surrounded by the Guanica Dry Forest. It's a bizarre landscape, and beautiful in an austere sort of way. Lots of cacti. If you're a hiker, go on line and print out maps of the forest trails. Also, go to TerraServer and look at the aerial photos of the terrain. Hiking into the hills is a great time. Pack lots of water and then add an extra bottle.-- Had a good and reasonably priced meal at the restaurant at the main Gilligan's Island ferry dock (not the resort's dock). They also sell emplanadas, or meat pies, which make a nice lunch on the island.-- You need a rental car because Copamarina is miles from anywhere. Invest in a good road map and study it. We traveled all around the southwestern quarter of Puerto Rico and made discovery after discovery. Beautiful beaches. Lighthouses. Views that took your breath away.-- If you go to the bioluminescent bay, expect to be disappointed. It is nothing like the firefly-glitter in the final scene of Lord of the Flies (if you happened to see the old movie). But, we were there on a moonless night, and the boat trip under the stars was well worth the price. I don't know that I've ever seen more stars in a sky.-- Copamarina is on a narrow and torturous coastal road. (It is well paved with lines painted on the edges.) If you drive to the end of the road, there is a lovely but littered public beach. If you're a hiker, take the trail that follows the coast beyond the road's end. You'll be rewarded with dramatic views. There are not many places where you can walk for miles along the ocean and see no one else. Again, take lots of water. Also be forewarned: There were male prostitutes at the beach itself trolling for clients.-- If you get the craving, there's a Burger King in Guanica at the intersection to the highway leading to Copamarina. Come to think of it, there's a MacDonalds nearby, too.-- Copamarina is a place to unwind, relax, read books, play tennis. There is no nightlife. By 10 o'clock or so, the resort is asleep. Know what you're getting into, and you'll love it.

<Author>jwhiteree
<Content>Great Place to take Kids! We spent the week before Easter at the Copamarina with our two boys, ages 8 and 6.5. We all had a fantastic time and would go back in a heartbeat.We rented a car in San Juan and drove to the resort. I highly recommend having a rental car. It is a long drive to Guanica, but very pretty. The other drivers are crazy, so be prepared. It is easy to get lost in PR because the roads are not marked well. You are best to know what town you want to go to next. There are signs that direct you to a town so you will have to go by that.The resort never seemed crowded. Sometimes we had to wait a little bit for a table at breakfast, but only if we got there later in the morning. Go early and you are fine. You need to prepare for the slower pace. If you are used to BAM BAM BAM service, things are a little different. And this is not just at Copamarina. Even Burger King is slow. It is just the way it is, so relax about it and enjoy. You are supposed to be vacationing anyway.The boat ride out to Gulligan's Island was not running. GI is/was closed, but the boat captain will take you out to Playa Ballena instead. Very worth it. (You can drive to Ballena by going down 333 past the resort, but take the boat. It puts you way out at the point where it is not crowded.) You will find a Caribbean beach with no one on it if you walk out to the point and around. Go to the dive shop and they will radio the boat to come to the resort dock and pick you up.The countryside is rather depressing. A lot of run down homes and buildings and wandering mangy dogs. I was told by a local, why put a lot of effort into your house? Hurricane is going to come knock it down every few years anyway... But look past that, and you will find wonderful kind people who are very accomidating. We only ran into 4 people the entire week who did not speak any English. If you plan on driving around, get a guidebook that has some common Spanish-all the street signs are in Spanish. My husband thought there was this town named Salida which all roads seemed to lead to. I told him, NO, salida means exit silly!Our room was very nice. We did not do all inclusive, so we only ate in the fancypants resort rest. one night. Our meal was okay. For the four of us, the bill came to $130 (that is with 2 kids w/meals from the kids' menu). Someone else mentioned in a review to stay away from local food. I disagree! Do some research and understand what you are eating, and you will find it quite good. We discovered Pinchos, which are basically chicken or pork on a stick, grilled with BBQ or Hot sauce. LOVE THEM! There is a vendor that sells them on the waterfront walk in Guanica. $1 each. We ate our last night in PR for $6 the four of us. There is a very good pizza place in Guanica called cleverly, Guanica Pizza. Ask at the front desk. They have info. The pizza place will deliver to the resort. We paid $16 for two medium pizzas that would be called larges back in the States.We did day trips to El Yunque and Arecibo and Camuy. It is quite an effort to get anywhere on the island. Plan on a whole day, but it is worth it. A drive to La Paragua just west of Guanica (which is where the bioluminescent bay is) is a good evening trip. We did the boat ride, unfortunately on a full moon night, so the bay was not very good. But we paid $20 for the 4 of us to have a hour+ after dinner moonlight boat ride, and that was fantastic. There were oodles of other kids for our boys to play with. All Puerto Rican children seem to speak perfect English thanks to cable T.V. The resort staff had organized activites for kids every day, and the guy who led them was FANTASTIC! It is true the beach is not a crashing ocean beach. The resort is in a cove, and the bottom is silty with grass. Cana Gorda, a public beach is a 2 minute walk down the shore and is a great place for swimming, but even here, the waves are not huge. The waves break way offshore on the reefs, so leave your surfboard at home. There are vendors at Cana Gorda where you can get cheap eats and $1 Medalla beers.If you have a car, there is a dirt road off 333 that goes down a cliff on the right side heading back to the resort. There is a green gate. This leads down to Playa Jaboncillo. GO THERE! The road is a little rutty and steep, but we got our Scion down there and back up just fine. At the bottom there is a gorgeous cove beach with cliff sides and no one there. Also drive down past the resort and there are more beaches, but go on a weekday. The locals flock to the beaches, and the areas around them are worn down and sometimes a lot of trash. Very sad, but try not to think about it. (I live on the East Coast and have been to VA Beach and Ocean City MD, and there they have to sift the trash out of the sand every night! Can't stand those places!)The ONLY bad thing that happened was the snorkeling trip on the dive boat. For our last day, we had made a reservation to go out on the snorkeling trip at $45 a head. It just so happened that I stopped by the dive shop that morning and happened to overhear that there was a problem with the boat, and the trip for the day was canceled. I was a little put off that they had not contacted us and told us. I asked the people in the dive shop what was going on, and they were very evasive, like they were hiding something. Was the boat broken? Problem with the Coast Guard? No one would really say. (The Coast Guard was there for some reason.) I told them that I would like to know b/c it is our last day, and I did not want to waste it. It ended up that the trip was canceled, so we went to Playa Jaboncillo instead and had a wonderful last day after all.I would go back to Copamarina without a second thought. If you want to plop at the resort and not move, get the all inclusive. If you like to go travel and see things, have a car. If you have kids, they will LOVE it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Relax and Enjoy Copamarina This is my second visit to copamarina, I went two years ago in the winter. I traveled with My husband, mother, father and a four year old and we loved it. There was so much to do except for the evenings. Guanica is a quiet town and there was no night live at the hotel. So if that's what your looking for go elsewhere this is not the place for you. We had dinner at the Alexandra our first night and service was slow. My mother and daughter was falling asleep while waiting. The food was good and compared to New York prices I didn't find them to be expensive, $26.00 for filet mignon and lobster tail, not bad. The breakfast buffet was very good, they had everything you can think of. Also the rooms had mini refrigerators, so you can stock up on snacks if you are on a budget.I was dissapointed to see that the Parrots that where once there were gone. According to the front desk visitors complained about the noise. Hello, we are in the carribean. That was part of the hotel's charm, my daughter was looking forward to seeing them. If you are traveling with kids, see Miguel at the dive shop. He plans activites daily for the kids and he is wonderful. I must say that the staff tried their best. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>pretty hotel, horrible beach We drove over 3 hours from San Juan airport to Copamarina, past beautiful mountains and pretty small water falls along with many old small houses with or without people in it. Along the way it scared me, it looked like an unsafe place to be in if your car broke down. I did not ever thought I would feel this way, but I did. Thank God when we got to Guanica near our hotel, there were three police station, one fire station and I felt relieved. Everytime we drove around the next couple days we saw police cars one after another, some pulled tourist people giving them tickets for speeding, while we spotted residential (beat up cars) with badly cracked windshields driving without being stopped. People driving 25-75 miles an hour unlimited speed, they cut in front of you without signaling. Where's the highway patrolmans, I keep asking myself. I hope we make it back with our little 3 year old home in one piece, I prayed. At night we drove into tiny streets just looking for a restaurant or souvenier shop, except to find gambling joints, people drunk standing around, houses with bars all over this entire island!!!! Now, I got depressed, I said to my husband this has got to get better. No more next time.Back to the hotel the activity desk clerk would not let us have the trip to Gilligans Island, told us and everyone that it is closed for the whole week. We reserved the ferry ($5.00) days ago with receipt and today it just got canceled, only the $45.00 trip is available to that island. Tomorrow we have to go home. We all looked at each other feeling angry, lied to and cheated, and felt that if we all (hotel guests) would spend more money we can go its not true. We're just stuck, so we decided to go to the other not-so-famous beach the ferry goes every hour. This made the activity guy really angry!!! He gave me a hard time borrowing our hotel life jacket, snorkling gears, etc. Everyone on the boat felt angry too.We added all-inclusive to our over price room the 3rd day. We were informed by the reservationist that the plan includes foods, drinks, gratuities. My husband and I asked twice about the gratuities, just to make sure so we wouldn't look stupid. They said that the only people you tip are the bell-boy and the bartenders. We felt unjust so each time we got served we tip a few bucks or more. The next day back to the same restaurants they ignored us. So I said maybe their employers cheated them, why are they not jolly anymore. All-in-all this 7 day trip was boring and the people here are lazy, because the service was incredibly very slow. Breakfact is buffet style, but you had to stand and wait (5-10 min.) to get seated. No exaggeration, lunch and dinner took alittle over an hour for food (even for take outs). We got sick of looking at the same crowd. Thank God we made it back home safe and not sick thats all that matters. Amen.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>This is a great place to escape Being a one-half Puerto Rican stuck in the midwest, I love to get back to the island and have some good beach time. The beach at this resort does have sea grass and is not for swimming. But anyone who complains about that needs to drink less, drink more, or walk 100 yards west to Playa Cana Gorda. The public beach there is fabulous for swimming and (especially if you aren't all-inclusive at the resort) the beers are $1.Our first night there was a Monday (we stayed until Thursday am) and it is true that during the week it is very relaxed. The restaurant is good for breakfast and lunch, but EXCELLENT for dinner. Each of our evenings at dinner, the same hostess took our reservation and seated us. Each time, she remembered our names and our room #. The first night, Raul, the bartender gave me 2 hand-rolled cigars and the owner had a few drinks with us.Let me tell you, the service here is great. Middle of the week and not crowded yet there was a server at the pool area. This resort is also recognized for its environmental awareness. One thing to keep in mind (whichever type you are--I am somewhere in between): Even though there is an all-inclusive option, this is not a party-hearty environment. You get your meals, you get your drinks. However, the bar opens at about noon and closes around 10:30 or 11. One thing about that. Some said the drinks were kinda watered down. I didn't find that to be the case at all. Like anyplace else, tip the bartender fairly well and make conversation.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>paradise We wanted a quiet place where we could sit on the beach, gaze at the sea and get some sunshine on our pale, northern bodies. This was just right! The Copamarina has comfortable, clean rooms; a friendly, accomodating, laid-back staff; gorgeous landscaping and pools; and a nice, quiet beach. The dinners at Alexandra's were delicious, too. We had not expected much after reading other reviews, and were pleasantly surprised! Dinners were no more expensive than dining here, and by stressing that we wanted our meat very rare it was perfect.The beach does have grass in the water, and the bottom is a bit squishy in places, but it's not off-putting or unpleasant. Do get to the beach early to get one of the big beds, they're very cool, make you feel like royalty. We should have gone with the all-inclusive plan, since we never wanted to leave! We did take a trip up to Areciebo and took a scenic route instead of Highway 10; took all day but we saw beautiful countryside and many small villages.Weekends are very busy, lots of families  kids, so if kids bother you, choose somewhere else. But if you want a relaxing, sunshine-filled, lazy vacation at a reasonable price, the Copa is the place - we plan on returning!

<Content>Oasis Cold and windy in San Juan so rented a car and drive south into the calm sun. Arrived 2/15/05 and stayed 2 nites and really enjoyed the interlude. Probably the quietest facility we have ever visited.Beautiful grounds and nice rooms with unusual windows that we opened to the sea breezes. On a bay with wonderful sailing-rented a hobicat. There was one coin operated washing machine and dryer (handy!), and a small work out area and spa. Spent one evening in La Parguera and took the $5 tour of the bay-probably a victim of it's success-not many sparkly plankton left, but $5 worth of diversion, to be sure. We had no problems driving once we left San Juan and everyone matched our Spanish with their English, with grace. This is probably more of a vacation spot for those who live on the island, but we really enjoyed it!

<Author>mlwebb03
<Content>Wonderful Honeymoon We went to the Copamarina in July 2004 for our honeymoon as a part of a town and country package through the Hotel El Convento in San Juan. By far, the Copamarina was the better half of the package. It's hard to know where to begin in talking about the wonderful things they had there...the grounds are breathtaking, the staff is outgoing and friendly, and the food was excellent. Our room was minimally decorated, but we don't go on vacation to look at curtains and bedspreads anyway, and it was very clean. We went snorkeling through the resort's program, and it was great. We were the only two people snorkeling. We laid around in the hammocks they have strewn about the grounds, the sun beds, the lounge chairs, and felt fully pampered and relaxed. It was everything we could have wanted in a honeymoon.The only caveats I would add are that if you go, you really should get the all inclusive package, and rent a car. The food is very good, but I can imagine that we would have been upset if we'd been paying as we went. As it was, we were able to have all of the daquiris and margaritas we had fantasized about during February in Connecticut while we were planning our honeymoon, and enjoy a wide sampling of food at every meal without ever thinking of the price. Also, we found Guanica a good hub for exploring the dry forest, the rain forest, Ponce, and the bioluminescent bay, but having a car was necessary for that. Overall, I would highly recommend this resort to nature lovers (it's a green resort) and couples or families looking for rest and relaxation.

The room is decorated in tropical colors, large beautiful bathroom, wooden shutters to the deck or patio, good a/c and an adequate television. The maid staff was efficient and the rooms cleaned daily (we tipped daily, and our room seem to be cleaned very well), the gardens, pool areas and beach seemed to always be clean without seeing lot of cleaning activity. The gardens and pool areas are very large and uncrowded. The resort has a lot of acreage for the small number of rooms (approx. 120 rooms). There was never a problem getting lounges at the pool or beach. Besides chairs and lounges on the beach there are also a number of large futons - yes futons on the beach. One is on a low wooden platform, the other two are on raised frames with drapes that you can pull closed all around for privacy, including a drape on top to protect from the sun. Great for a nap on the beach or more?? We did not take advantage of these.There is a dive shop/gift shop on the beach with dive and snorkel trips gear, towels. They also have kayaks, paddle boats and some other available watercraft.Everything up till the edge of the water is top shelf. The ocean water comes up short. It is very shallow, very grassy and kind of like clay bottom. So going to this resort to use the great beach would be a disappointment, but knowing this limitation leaves you options to either sit on the beach (great breezes and the sound of the water lapping on the sand) and swimming in the pool, while exploring the island for great beaches (of which we found many). There is also a public beach just a short walk away - it was a little better, not much. I did a little snorkeling on the far end of that beach.We were on the all inclusive in that we were on a timeshare exchange through RCI, which was mandatory all inclusive. The A/I includes all meals, beverages and 1 hour of non motorized boat daily.The Food: Breakfast was served begining at 7:00 and went to 11:00.While most people raved about the food, we are not quite as big of fans as others. First the positives; the staff was nice, friendly and a good resource to find things to do off of the resort. Breakfast was buffet on weekends, off the menu during the week. Fruit quality and selection was a bit of a disappointment. There was always plenty to eat, but in general we found the food to be very inconsistant. The salmon one night was great the next dried out. We found many of the entrees at Alexanders (the dinner, white tablecloth restaurant) dried out. Maybe it was just a temporary issue with help, but it wasn't a wow. With that said it is the only show in town, there are no other restaurants or night spots nearby. The prices at Alexanders were very high off the menu, making the all inclusive a deal. Although not thrilled with it it was fine and recommended.The desk staff was very helpful and friendly.Things we did -1. walks in the dry forest, Take a left out of the resort at a green gate on the left side of the road is a nice easy walk through the dry forest, spectacular flora and fauna. Walk up to the 400 year old tree. Continue down this road - beautiful beaches. One day we took a drive to the main area of dry forest and took a short hike there. Lots of butterflies.2- La Paguera - Bio Luminescent bay trip. 35 minutes from resort this $5.00 trip was a minor event, but fun non the less. Very few tourists on the boat, Cute fishing village worth checking out. We had a highlight when we ran into a parade heading right towrds us. We pulled over and watched as many tows people in marching bands, baton twirlers and dancers came marching by with the ever present speaker trucks blasting native music. What fun !!!3- Long day trip seeking out beaches in Isabella, Aquadera (sp?) and Rincon. Found (with much persistance) Shacks Beach in Isabella !! Great Snorkelling !!. Continued down the road to find many other cool beaches. Not thrilled with Crashboat Beach, although it is written up many places as a top beach. Don't miss Rincon's beaches - good snorkeling on Tres Palms and watching the surfers on Dome's Beach was fun. Leaving Domes Beach on the right is a great little gift and t-shirt shop, fun proprietor and great shirts.Finding our way in and out of the towns and to the beaches was a challenge. Buy yourself a good road map before you go, and you still will need a good sense of direction and sense of humor. Coming back from Rincon we ended up going up and down over imposing mountains with two way streets only wide enough for one and a half cars. STAY RIGHT!!!! We ran into roads like these all over the island, with amny local drivers of trucks and cars alike driving on either side of the road.4- We also, took in (on the recommendation of a waiter) a local Christmas light display in a neighborhood in Jancoa. Ask and find fun local things to do.The highlight of the trip was on our last day we got up at 5:30 to make the long 3hr drive to Fajardo and took a high speed catamaran to Culabra. We went with East Winds. Great fun trip on a cool boat to a reef for snorkeling in the most vibrant colorful and alive area I have ever seen under water. They then took us to Flamengo Beach, all I can say is PARADISE. Rated one of the top three beaches in all of the world on many services. They also fed us lunch, fruit and beverages including rum punches. Good people, great trip at a fair price.We had a greta time in Puerto Rico and just scratched the surface. We could go back multiple times and still find new things to do and explore.

<Author>FamilyGuy-CT
<Content>Great for quiet family vacation We were at the Copamarina for five nights in the first week of December and had a great time. We are a family of 4 - two boys 5yr and 1yr. This was our first trip to Puerto Rico.On reaching puerto rico, we spent 3 nights in San Juan. In spite of being warned, we were surprised by the size of the urban sprawl. We were very happy to move to the quiet part of the island and spend 5 days at Copamarina.The resort is very nice. Grouds are well taken care of. The rooms are spacious and they either have a balcony or patio. The staff was very friendly and helpful. They started to decorate the place for christmas when we were there and it made the place look even nicer.The kids really enjoyed their time in the pool, the beach and the lawns. My 5yr old was not happy with the sea grass and made a big fuss about going into the water. Kids will probably only play on the sand or at the water's edge - not swim. Upside - water is very calm, like a small lake.The people at the dive shop were excellent. Very friendly. Happy to take care of any special needs. I just went for one short dive on the local reef ( about 2miles from resort ). Nice reef, wide variety of fish. From the dock, you can also take a boat to a beach ($5 round trip) which can only be reached by boat. It is white sand and next to a small mangrove islands. Great for snorkeling as the water visibility was excellent. The fact that we could do all this from a dock just steps from the room was a huge plus for us.The only problem we had was that the place lost electricity for a little bit on the last evening. The generators got most of the lights on. But, perhaps unrelated, the water stopped as well. We were told that this was due to a major problem at the water company and that 3-4 local towns were affected. The next morning, we still had no water. As we were checking out early, we got the staff (still friendly) to give us some water in the ice bucket to brush our teeth, etc. I guess something like this could happen anywhere. I wouldnt blame the hotel. But, if we had to suffer this for 1 or 2 days, I suppose I wouldnt be that generous.The resort also seemed less than half full. I think that made our experience that much more relaxed. but, we loved it and would certainly consider going back again.

<Author>memcc
<Content>Nice spot The Copamarina is a 1.5 hour beautiful drive from the San Juan Airport. On your way, be on the lookout for the white monument to the puerto rican farmer - this is the only spot to pull over and photograph the beautiful valley that you will see all the way along route 2. If you miss it, it's a royal pain to turn around.The Copamarina has very nice grounds and a cute little dive shop and pier. We were there in early October, so still off-season. Almost all of the rooms are ocean view, so it was easy to be given one. The room had a very tropical cabana feel to it with rattan furniture and a tiled floor, wooden shutters onto the balcony - but it also was air conditioned, with running water (beautiful blue tiled full-length shower stall) and a large tv. Don't forget to ask for your safe key at the desk - there is a $25 deposit and if you forget you have to walk all the way back.Since we were there in the off-season there wasn't a lot going on. We took a taxi boat from the pier to a local beach that was a little clearer than the beach at the hotel (somewhat turbulent water and many grassy patches). That was $5 apiece round trip. We were hoping to go to Guilligan's Island but due to Hurricane Jeanne it was shut down completely.We drove in to Ponce. Do not do this without getting explicit directions to the tourist section/old town. We never found it and had a disappointed dinner at a Taco Maker at a truck stop on the way back to the hotel.DO go into Parguera and charter a little motor boat to take you snorkelling. We did this for $25 an hour - a small boat with canopy and a captain all to ourselves - we recommend Johnny Boat - the 'captain' was very sweet and insisted on using up the full two hours that we paid for (after seeing many many jelly fish, though the snorkelling was great, we were ready to head in) - and took us to iguana island to see the wild iguanas which are accustomed to being fed by tourists.No problems with the hotel, aside from cleaning the pools at seemingly inopportune times, and poor signage regarding that fact so that we were covered in slimey drying chlorine before realizing what was wrong with the water...

<Author>arlyjb
<Content>Excellent food My husband and I just returned from 5 days at the Copamarina Resort in Puerto Rico. Expedia never forwarded our reservation to the hotel, but the staff was so helpful and caring sorting it out for us. Thankfully I brought the email confirmation with us. The Copamarina on the southwest coast of PR is on the Caribbean. The resort is lovely, with two large pools, 2 kiddie pools and a nice beach. The water is grassy in patches but it's not a problem. The public beach is easily accessible right next to the resort. The rooms are good sized, immaculate and painted peach and green. The Copamarina has the most amazing food of any all inclusive that we've ever stayed at. Lobster tail (large ones!), red snapper stuffed with lobster, crab and shrimp and filet mignon that melts in your mouth are just a few of the dishes offered. The staff are mostly university students from the local college who speak English and are very friendly. We hated to leave and look forward to returning.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I enjoyed the Copamarina Our group flew into Puerto Rico and arrived into beautiful weather in San Juan. We were met by the hotel shuttle, which was waiting directly outside the airport. The drive from San Juan to the Copamarina took about two hours. In future visits, we would probably see if we could get a flight to Mayaguez or Ponce, both of which are only a half-hour away from the resort.The resort was small, but well-situated. It's located in a protected bay, so there were very few waves on the beach. The water was comfortably warm, but the beach itself was covered largely with seagrass rather than sand. This wasn't too big of an issue, although my wife was stung by something in the grass at one point (plant or animal we don't know). Since the water was calm, swimming in the bay was nice.The rooms were large and comfortable, with a sitting area next to the bed. The inclusion of a refrigerator was nice. The bathrooms were adequate, nothing special. As someone else mentioned, the rooms could use some soundproofing. The honeymooners next door were...energetic.Having arrived via airport shuttle rather than a rental, we stayed at the resort for the entire six days we were there. As a result, we ate all of our meals at the resort. We didn't mind it too much, although I wish the menu had been a little more diverse. We purchased the all-inclusive plan for all of our meals, so we weren't bothered by the menu prices and didn't feel the need to watch our pennies at the bar. Thus, while the prices looked a bit high, we figured, with what we ate and drank, and with daytime trips to the bar, that we all broke even.The crowd at the hotel was mixed between adult couples and families. Not so many kids that it was annoying, but enough so that we occasionally got splashed at our poolside table by rambunctious children. Our days were spent mostly sitting on the beach or near one of the pools reading. Bar service was maybe not speedy, but acceptable. Service at the restaurants was a bit on the slow side, but we were on vacation so it was okay. The one potential complaint: When we made our reservations we asked if they had laundry service and they said they did. When we asked for laundry service a few days later, they said they didn't do that. However, when we complained about this, somebody from the hotel staff did do our laundry, so they made it right. All in all, it was a great relaxing vacation. We would probably go back, but we'd try to get a flight to somewhere closer to the resort to avoid the two hour drive. Also, we might want to rent a car to try some other restaurants, since by the end of our trip our group had run through the menu more than once.

With or without the emergency, I would recommend this resort to anyone who would consider going to Puerto Rico. It is top notch!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Great Quiet Place to Relax We purchased a week at Copamarina via Expedia. What a great choice!!! It is around 2hr drive from San Juan, so you need a rental. It makes more sense to rent a car than to take hotel transportation from the airport, and does not cost that much more. The drive itself is worth getting a rental. If you like aggressive driving, Puerto Rico is an ideal place; drivers are determined and 'take chances' all the time, but are quite skilled. Driving down from San Juan, you will pass the mountains, which offer excellent views and an exciting drive. The resort itself is in a very secluded area, in a wonderful and famous dry forest, located right on a warm bay. Even though it rains around the area quite a bit, the resort stays dry and sunny due to being enclosed by adjacent hills. The beach/ocean is grassy. But, you can walk 5 min to an always empty public beach with nice sand and even nicer water. Or you can take a boat trip (15 min) to one of the islands and enjoy the beaches there ($8 round trip). The resort offers a free breakfast (from 7 to 11, IIRC) that is a very nice outdoors buffet with great choices of food, fruit, and beverages. The pools are nice and clean, and the area is very green and grassy. The rooms are not very big, but nice and clean. The bathrooms are also very pleasant. Remember to bring ear plugs if you need complete silence to sleep well. Sound proofing is poor, but that is the way buildings are build in the tropic. The people at the resort are very friendly and accommodating, from ground keepers to receptionists. Ask the manager to use the internet (6pm is the best time to get a PC), there is no wireless internet connection at the resort. If you have a car, take a trip to Phosphorus Bay. Also, devote 1 day to visiting El Yunke, the only tropical forest in North America (or its Commonwealth). But watch out for cops (speed traps are almost as common as in the upper 48), speeders are heavily fined (paid $130 for 26mph over the limit), but reckless driving is not a problem... as long as you are not speeding. If you are up to spending another day on the road, go to the Arecibo Observatory, the largest observatory in the US (and a recent James Bond movie was filmed there too). Shopping areas are close by, with a grocery store and a K-mart, and many neat restaurants/fast food joints that are about 20 min away (by car). And of course check out Old San Juan!!! All in all, we were very pleased with the resort, and Puerto Rico; a beautiful island with great climate and friendly people. Copamarina is an affordable, clean, sort-of upscale, and relaxing resort that is working hard to be even better. Go and visit, and find out for yourself!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful resort My twelve-year-old daughter and I just arrived home from spending the last week in March at the Copamarina and I highly recommend it. The resort itself is lovely, beautifully landscaped with two pools, two kiddie pools and two jacuzzis. We had the breakfast buffet included in our room rate which was a good deal since it was $18 per person ($12 for children) when not included in the room charge. We often had lunch at the poolside restaurant and had dinner there several nights, sitting outside listening to the wonderful guitarist. The service, contary to what others have written here, was consistently efficient, pleasant and professional. The dinner menu was on the expensive side but the prices are typical of meals at quality resorts and there are plenty of other restaurants within a half hour to 45 minute drive. The beach is lovely but the swimming there is quite limited by very shallow water and lots of sea grass--fine for wading but not really swimming and definitely not snorkling right from the beach. We rented a car and left the resort for sightseeing just about every day as there are spectacular beaches, beautiful scenery, delicious restaurants in nearby towns, but you will have to drive to see them and just plan to take the time to get there. One of the reasons the Copamarina is wonderful is that it is a hidden jewel--not overrun with people and not touristy, just a quality resort secuded in a wonderful part of the island. Also contary to what others have said here, the resort is not difficult to find and the drive from San Juan is quite easy, taking about 90 minutes to 2 hours. In short, great resort, ideal for families and couples alike.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very Quiet We just got back from the Copamarina in Guanica. We rented a car at the Airport which I highly recommend since it is abut a 2 hour and 15 minute drive and same price as shuttle. When you leave the Airport take the exit onto the Tedoro Moscoso Bridge (the one with the american and puertorican flags on it) pay the toll this will lead you to route 17 stay in the right lane and follow thru traffic to the Caguas exit keep an eye out for it, this takes you onto the 52, follow all the way into ponce through Beautiful Scenery and Mountains, you will go tthru 5 tolls. Route 52 converts in Ponce to route 2 (on route 2 outside of Ponce there is Pito's Seafood on your left just past the El Tourque Water park this is an excellent restaurant with the freshest Lobster (ask for it to be grilled it was awesome) stay on 2 going past the town of Yauco (the best Coffee) you stay on 2 going past the Yauco plaza just past that take the exit #194 this exit will take you onto the 116 where at the 3rd light take a left by the Burger King, now you are on 333 in Guanica (rundown town watch out for the stray dogs) Here there is a Econo grocery by the McDonalds. on the 333 follow through the winding curves and Beautiful scenery of the cliffs and Ocean (it is Beautiful) this takes a little while as the roads are one lane. Follow down past the Cana Gorda Beach and Copamarina is on the right. The driving was beautiful and worth it. The drivers are a little wreckless so beware. The Hotel was pretty but very quiet, this really isnt a place for kids it is more like a place for retired people to vacation or people who just like to sit and be on the beach. The beach wasnt the greatest cause you cant really swim there, but a few steps down the beach to the Cana Gorda beach is perfect for swimming in the clear water. Look for sand crabs they are so cute and interesting to watch. The diving is great if you are an avid diver and the snorkeling at Gilligans Island was ok for $4 but the water wasnt real clear, but it is a beautiful white sand cay. If you have a car I suggest taking a right out of the Hotel and driving down the road to a beautiful and scenic area where you can play on a beautiful beach and bring a picnic, it was so beautiful there and private not many people. The Hotel is quiet with no night life, the food is exspensive (but the rooms have fridges so that was nice we got groceries from the Econo grocery store in Guanica) The Breakfast was not very good and it was $14 per person, so we went to McDonalds and got the same stuff for $7 for the both of us. We had an Ocean front room (room 115) it was pretty and the deck was nice to relax in. We got a lot of rest, so if you want to just rest and do a little then stay here because the scenery down there is beautiful. If you want nightlife stay in San Juan, it is dirty there but there is a lot of Bars. My husband and I liked it here but we dont think we will go back as it was too quiet. We love Playa Del Carmen Mexico a lot better and got a lot more for our money and there was more to do and more shops. We hardly brought anything back but Rum (which isnt all bad) but I wanted to buy more trinkets for our kids.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>One of the best spots in Puerto Rico! Just returned from a fabulous week at the Copamarina resort. We cannot say enough good things about this property, the amenities and the service.Location ? about ninety miles from San Juan. If you want to get away from the tourist scene, this is the place. Very easy drive on modern roadways, and the directions are simple to follow. A few 35 cent tolls on Rt. 52 so have some change handy.The cost of the rental car for the week is roughly the same as the hotel shuttle fee for two people, so I recommend renting so you can explore the surrounding area.Property ? beautifully groomed, tastefully appointed grounds. While the beach is rather shallow, there is more than enough space to enjoy your privacy, and the property abuts a very nice public beach with plenty of deep water swimming. Two large pools, hot tubs, fountains, etc.Surrounding area ? you are in a remote part of the country. There are supermarkets, etc. approximately a ten minute drive away, but there is very little in the way of nightlife or alternative restaurants, shopping etc. Ponce is 40 minutes away, with a casino, etc. but that is not why you would choose this property for a vacation.We did spend a day driving around to the different towns, beaches, dry forest preserve, etc. and there is plenty to see.Facilities ? health club, water sports, dive shop, etc. are all on-site and staffed by very helpful people. Snorkeling out on Gilligan?s island ($4 ferry ride) is a great way to spend the day.Room ? large, airy, tropical. We stayed in a Superior Gardenview, which was quite large and spacious and tastefully decorated. The ocean-facing wall is fitted with wooden shutters with screens, so you can let in the fresh breezes all evening (privacy is not a problem). Refrigerators  safes are provided.Restaurant  bar ? food is fresh, plentiful and well prepared. Highly recommend the all-inclusive plan, which enables you to eat  drink anything on the menus for all meals throughout the entire day. To keep things simple, we tipped our dinner server each evening, and took care of the other members of the wait staff (same people who served us throughout each day) at the end of our stay.The bar area closes around sunset on weekdays, but drinks are available through the restaurant (until 10:30 p.m. or so) and there is a courtyard area with live music each night.Service ? can?t say enough. Most service people tended to be quiet  non-intrusive (a good thing), but this approach could be misinterpreted by those wanting for the obnoxious Disney-like doting. Initiate the conversation and you?ll find that each member of the staff is delightful and more than willing to meet your every need. Example: Sunday night around 7:30 p.m. we stopped off at the front desk to inform them that our shower would need repair the following day but was not urgent; it was fixed by the time we returned from dinner.Recommendation ? if you are looking to get away for a few days to lie in the sun, eat well, do nothing, swim, snorkel, kayak and otherwise lounge about, this is the place. We will return again next winter.

<Content>Paradise flawed....pack a lunch The trip to the Copa, although just over 90 miles, took 2-1/2 hours to reach. Directions were adequate but traffic, road construction, highway closures (couldn't determine why) really slowed us down. Drivers on highways, especially, are quite aggressive. Be prepared for lots of stray, malnourished dogs along the twisty road to the resort. We started buying bags of dog food to drop off - some kind person provided a jug of water.Ah, yes, the Copa! Incredible spot to relax, unwind and forget about cold New England winter. However, there's no beach...the grassy waters off the 'beach' harbor all sorts of critters who really don't like being stepped on! Two pools are quite wonderful. Restaurants (2) are incredibly overpriced and food quality is marginal - processed turkey in a turkey club sandwich - $13.00. Unless you rent a car, you're stuck - there's nothing accessible by foot and we never found anything suitable during our 7 days there.Would we go again? NO We found the island outrageously beautiful but dirty, noisy and not real welcoming. Full of potential, but it seems there's lack of ambition to improve the resort - or much else.

<Author>milomannn
<Content>This place is a treasure! This beach resort was a true pleasure to stay at. We used the internet to find it but when we arrived, I was surprised at how luxurious the grounds and rooms were. Now for specifics: It is located in a remote section of south western PR. The terrain of the area is dry and scrub, but there is a beauty in the natural landscape. The resort is surrounded by a UN forest preserve with many trails. We saw butterflies and birds during our hikes. The resort grounds are garden like and lush. Although we were told that the resort was full, you never got the feeling that it was crowded. The beach is mediocre for swimming (low and sea grass beds) but next door was a better public beach and within a short drive were the more lovely natural beaches within the forest preserve. The staff was very friendly, helpful and usually bilingual. We were a family of four and had two rooms which were very large and comfortable for our seven day stay. It doesn't matter if you have a garden view or water view but I would suggest asking for the second floor if you like privacy and the ground floor if you want your kids to have quick easy access to the pool and walkways. The all inclusive plan is certainly well worth the money. It gives you 3 meals plus all drinks (alcoholic or non) at any time and one hour of non motorized water equipment usage. Also there are practically no restaurants within easy driving distance but if you wanted to explore beyond 30 minutes or farther, you probably could find some. As a result of the all inclusive plan we probably did not see as much of the area as I would have liked but lounging around seemed to be our agenda this time. The only complaint all four of us had was how slow the service at the restaurant was. Some servers were very efficient but others left you waiting. We would have no problem go back again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A perfect paradise getaway at the copamarina I loved copamaraina. At first I thought what a lousy place moisquitos everywhere, and long lines at check in. If you go you can easily prove my first theory wrong. The rooms are clean and nice and cool. In fact i was freezing! I soon realized i hadn't had lunch and glanced at the map and headed down to Las Pamlas Cafe. Just a short walk away from my room I had a delicious meal which was costly, but worth it. Also the resort has a ferry which leads to Gilligan's Island a great place to go snorkeling with the family. The water was clear however I did not find an fish which I particularly liked. By sitting by the beach at sunset on the resort you can see a beautiful display of vibrant colors. The resort has a few pools, some for the kids, some for you and fun for the whole family. If your more of an athletic person you can try the tennis courts which are open till 10:00 p.m. Copamarina also rents you tennis raquets, scuba equipment, flippers and snorkeling masks, they also give you towels to use at the pool or at any water sport. The only bad thing is that is if you weren't planning on eating at the resturaunts provided by the resort I suggest leaving quite early because it will be awhile till you find a decent resturaunt. Age-10

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We loved it here! We loved our stay at the Copamarina! My husband and I and our 16 month old son travel to Puerto Rico at least twice a year and have stayed at many resorts and small inns throughout the island. Now that we are parents we especially seek places that are family friendly. Our room was spacious and clean. (The resort supplies cribs upon request) Our room was an ocean-view room and near the main pool and kiddie pool which was really nice and convenient. There are great garden paths that our son loved to walk along and explore and smell the local flowers! There are two great kiddie pools which my son absolutely loved and didn't want to come out of, and the ocean is calm and great for kids to play as well. The resort is clean, the grounds immaculate, and the staff is very nice and helpful. I do agree with some of the other reviews that state the food is expensive. We thought it was too. The upside is that the rooms have mini-fridges so we stopped at a local supermarket and stocked up on fresh bread, cold cuts, drinks and snacks and we'd eat lunch out on our room patio everyday. (We bought the package where our breakfast was included so that took care of that meal. Well worth it since it was great rolling out of bed and being served a nice hot breakfast before hitting the pool and beach!) For dinner we'd get into our rental car and explore the island where we found some fantastic and really inexpensive restaurants that served local island food. All in all, we highly recommend this resort and plan on returning in the near future!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Quiet and overpriced The place is just OK. I think it carries some intrinsic value for local people and that is what drives the price. I have no other explanation why I paid 220+ per night. Overall, the only reason to be there is it's quietness.The worst? MOSQUITOES!!! Early in the morning and right after dark especially after rain.The rooms are just OK and room service is mediocre. I had much better rooms at Dominican at half price. Breakfast menu is very limited and costs you $16. Open air lunch restaurant is better but closes too early. Drinks are a bit expensive. Dinner at the only restaurant is good and expensive, the service is low class. They just do not know what they are doing and do not understand you. There is nothing to do after dark. The beach is shallow and clogged with some kind of grass. The pools are nice, maybe too small. There are two pools for kids and sort of a playground.The surroundings are pretty and wild. We didn't see the trails, which I will always regret.If you still decide to go there, get a car in San Juan and keep it. Everyone we met there did that and no one ate at their restaurant more then once. Local village has a very simple restaurant, Blue Marlin.
